4:77:1694:20:14:85:515:627:144:Times:144:Times:C:The  European  Union  is  legally  entitled  to  the  revenue  from  (1)  agricultural  and  sugar  
4:78:1794:14:14:85:513:613:144:Times:144:Times:C:levies, (2) customs duties, (3) a 1 percent rate on each Member States' value added tax 
4:79:1882:14:14:85:513:599:144:Times:144:Times:C:base, and (4) a resource on the basis of GNP. Currently, the Union is actively involved 
4:80:1970:14:14:85:513:585:144:Times:144:Times:C:in the search for a fifth own revenue source. Therefore, the European Commission (DG 
4:81:2055:14:14:85:514:571:144:Times:144:Times:C:XIX) has invited the authors to trace 'who pays the taxes'. As requested, our report gives 
4:82:2146:14:14:85:514:557:144:Times:144:Times:C:a  general  account  of  methods  to  investigate  impacts  of  taxation.  More  specifically,  we  
4:83:2246:14:14:85:514:543:144:Times:144:Times:C:have estimated the incidence of national tax systems (Germany, the Netherlands, Spain 
4:84:2332:14:14:85:514:529:144:Times:144:Times:C:and the United Kingdom), and the incidence of present own resources and prospective 
4:85:2416:14:14:85:516:515:144:Times:144:Times:C:new  (tax)  resources  of  the  European  Union.  Up  till  now,  such  information  was  not  
4:86:2511:14:14:85:179:501:144:Times:144:Times:C:(readily) available.

4:91:2630:32:20:85:184:413:144:Times:144:Times:C:Zusammenfassung 
4:92:2646:20:14:85:516:393:144:Times:144:Times:C:Der  Europäischen  Union  werden  gesetzlich  folgende  Einnahmearten  zugeschrieben:  
4:93:2733:14:14:85:515:379:144:Times:144:Times:C:(1)  aus  Agrarabschöpfungen,  (2)  aus  Zöllen,  (3)  Mehrwertsteuer-Eigenmittel  und  (4)  
4:94:2826:14:14:85:518:365:144:Times:144:Times:C:BSP-Eigenmittel.   Gegenwärtig   sucht   die   Europäische   Union   nach   einer   fünften   
4:95:2920:14:14:85:514:351:144:Times:144:Times:C:Eigenmittelquelle.  Daher  hat  die  Europäische  Kommission  (DG  XIX)  die  Autoren  des  
4:96:3012:14:14:85:514:337:144:Times:144:Times:C:vorliegenden Beitrags aufgefordert, zu der Frage 'Wer bezahlt die Steuern?' Stellung zu 
4:97:3100:14:14:85:517:323:144:Times:144:Times:C:nehmen.  Unser  Bericht  stellt  zunächst  einmal  die  Methoden  zur  Erforschung  der  
4:98:3189:14:14:85:517:309:144:Times:144:Times:C:Steuerwirkungen  dar.  Insbesondere  haben  wir  das  Aufkommen  und  die  Verteilung  
4:99:3276:14:14:85:514:295:144:Times:144:Times:C:nationaler Steuersysteme (Deutschland, Niederlande, Spanien und Großbritannien), der 
4:100:3361:14:14:85:513:281:144:Times:144:Times:C:jetzigen EU-Eigenmittel und der zukünftigen Quellen der EU geschätzt. Bis jetzt waren 
4:101:3447:14:14:85:324:267:144:Times:144:Times:C:Informationen dieser Art nicht direkt zugänglich.

5:122:4011:19:20:72:401:627:12:Times:12:Times:B: WHO PAYS THE TAXES?

5:147:4241:18:0:72:219:174:12:Times:12:Times:B:Groningen, 15 November 1995 
7:148:4269:0:18:72:174:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:Executive summary 
7:149:4286:18:18:72:75:736:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
7:150:4286:18:18:72:135:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:Introduction 
7:151:4298:18:18:72:497:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:The European Union is legally entitled to the revenue from (1) agricultural and sugar levies, (2) 
7:152:4396:18:18:72:508:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:customs duties, and (3) a 1 percent rate on each Member States' value added tax base. As from 
7:153:4490:18:18:72:514:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:1988 the Union can call on a fourth own resource, on the basis of GNP. As a consequence of the 
7:154:4585:18:18:72:497:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:Edinburgh agreement, the share of this resource is estimated to rise from 14 percent (1992) to 
7:155:4680:18:18:72:195:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:nearly 50 percent (1999).  
7:156:4706:18:18:72:525:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Currently, the Union is actively involved in the search for a fifth own revenue source. The European 
7:157:4809:18:18:72:513:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:Council has explicitly requested the Commission for a report concerning possible candidates for a 
7:158:4907:18:18:72:504:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:fifth own resource.1 New European taxes can be judged in the light of their contribution to a fair 
7:159:5006:18:18:72:516:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:overall distribution of revenues and expenditures. One precondition for evaluating both the fairness 
7:160:5107:18:18:72:492:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:of the present tax system of the Union and its Member States, and to assess proposals for its 
7:161:5201:18:18:72:517:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:reform, is adequate knowledge about social and economic impacts of existing taxes, notably about 
7:162:5298:18:18:72:514:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:the distribution of tax burdens within the European Union. However, as yet such information is not 
7:163:5397:18:18:72:153:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:readily available.  
7:164:5416:18:18:72:508:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Therefore, the European Commission (DG XIX) has invited the authors to trace "who pays the 
7:165:5509:18:18:72:490:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxes". As requested, our report gives a general account of methods to investigate impacts of 
7:166:5603:18:18:72:488:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxation. More specifically, we have estimated the incidence of national tax systems, and the 
7:167:5697:18:18:72:527:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:incidence of present own resources and prospective new (tax) resources of the European Union. Up 
7:168:5794:18:18:72:311:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:till now, such information was not (readily) available. 
7:169:5849:18:18:72:509:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:  National tax systems of Member States show great variety. The Commission has stipulated that 
7:170:5944:18:18:72:524:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:our analysis should cover at least three significant Member States. We have decided to include four, 
7:171:6045:18:18:72:515:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:i.e. - in alphabetical order - Germany, the Netherlands, Spain and the United Kingdom. Together, 
7:172:6142:18:18:72:379:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:these countries account for over fifty percent of GNP of the Union.  
7:173:6210:18:18:72:75:304:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
7:174:6210:18:18:72:138:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:Methodology 
7:175:6221:18:18:72:521:268:12:Times:12:Times:B:The incidence of a tax is measured by the reduction in real income which results from the imposition 
7:176:6322:18:18:72:519:250:12:Times:12:Times:B:of that tax. We want to establish who pays the taxes (statutory incidence) and who ultimately bears 
7:177:6422:18:18:72:524:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:the tax burden (economic incidence). Both tax distributions will differ, since individuals and firms are 
7:178:6526:18:18:72:294:214:12:Times:12:Times:B:inclined to shift taxes they must pay onto others.  
7:179:6577:18:18:72:471:196:12:Times:12:Times:B:  For this report, data on taxes households paid in the early 1990s have been taken from 
7:180:6666:18:25:72:523:178:12:Times:12:Times:B:government administrations and nation-wide representative surveys among households. In a number 
7:181:6762:25:9:72:219:153:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
7:182:6782:9:19:72:527:144:8:Times:11:Times:F:     1 See Article 10 of the Decision on new own resources by the European Council, dated 31 October 
7:183:6882:19:0:72:475:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:1994 (94/728/EG, Euratom), Journal officiel des Communautés européennes, No L 293/13.  
8:184:6970:0:18:72:525:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:of cases such data were run through a microanalytic model to simulate the amount households pay in 
8:185:7069:18:18:72:511:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:certain taxes. Given the limitations inherent to available microdata, it was not possible to calculate 
8:186:7172:18:18:72:180:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:the burden of all taxes.  
8:187:7197:18:18:72:496:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Once the statutory incidence of taxes has been established, their economic incidence may be 
8:188:7291:18:18:72:507:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:traced under a variety of assumptions. Although some progress has been made in recent years in 
8:189:7386:18:18:72:525:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:improving the methodology of tax analysis, economists still disagree about the economic incidence of 
8:190:7487:18:18:72:490:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:several of the most important taxes in national tax systems. Reflecting the state of the art, our 
8:191:7585:18:18:72:310:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:incidence assumptions are spelled out in section 6.3. 
8:192:7638:18:18:72:507:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Results are presented as tax shares of ten groups, each containing ten percent of all households 
8:193:7737:18:18:72:513:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:(`deciles'). Households have been ranked into deciles by increasing income. Thus, the ten percent 
8:194:7835:18:18:72:523:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:poorest households are located in the first decile, the ten percent richest households are found in the 
8:195:7939:18:18:72:135:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:tenth decile.

9:240:9407:18:18:72:500:228:12:Times:12:Times:B:The European Union collects the VAT-based contribution of its Member States by means of a 
9:241:9497:18:18:72:497:210:12:Times:12:Times:B:notional harmonized base, and not as part of value added tax actually paid by consumers. The 
9:242:9590:18:18:72:517:192:12:Times:12:Times:B:incidence of the VAT-based contribution will be reviewed when discussing the impact of new own 
9:243:9685:18:0:72:172:174:12:Times:12:Times:B:resources (table 0.5). 
10:244:9709:0:18:72:520:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:The incidence of the GNP-based own resources of the EU is in fact determined by the incidence of 
10:245:9806:18:18:72:504:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:national tax systems of Member States. Table 0.4 shows the economic incidence of national tax 
10:246:9900:18:18:72:210:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:systems of the four countries.  
10:247:9931:18:18:72:522:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:For a correct interpretation of the information contained in table 0.4 it is very important to note that, 
10:248:10037:18:18:72:508:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:due to missing data, the incidence of several taxes could not be traced. Given wide differences in 
10:249:10136:18:18:72:519:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:national tax mixes, taking into account the spread in taxes covered (62-98 percent of aggregate tax 
10:250:10236:18:18:72:524:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:revenue), and considering the substantial variation in GDP per capita (table 4.1) and in the inequality 
10:251:10340:18:18:72:502:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:of the distribution of household incomes, the pattern of tax incidence in the four Member States 
10:252:10437:18:18:72:265:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:included in our report is strikingly similar.   
10:253:10484:18:18:72:524:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The fifty percent poorest households carry 23-24 percent of the aggregate tax burden in Germany, 
10:254:10583:18:18:72:499:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:the Netherlands and Spain, whereas the ten percent with the highest incomes contribute 25-26 
10:255:10676:18:18:72:526:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:percent. Only in the United Kingdom, tax burdens are more skewed towards rich households, which 
10:256:10772:18:18:72:525:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:may perhaps be explained by the greater inequality of the personal income distribution in this country 
10:257:10875:18:18:72:265:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:and zero-rated items for VAT-purposes.

10:274:11305:18:18:72:509:233:12:Times:12:Times:B:In recent years, several proposals for new own EU resources have been fielded. We will assume 
10:275:11399:18:18:72:524:215:12:Times:12:Times:B:here that new own resources are introduced within a framework of revenue neutrality. It follows that 
10:276:11500:18:18:72:514:197:12:Times:12:Times:B:to judge the net impact of the introduction of any new resource the incidence of this new resource 
10:277:11599:18:18:72:499:179:12:Times:12:Times:B:and the incidence of the present resource it (partly) replaces should be jointly considered. One 
10:278:11696:18:18:72:499:161:12:Times:12:Times:B:proposal aims at the introduction of an own VAT-resource to finance part of the outlays of the 
10:279:11791:18:18:72:484:143:12:Times:12:Times:B:Union. It is assumed here that the distribution of this tax would closely resemble the present 
10:280:11886:18:0:72:526:125:12:Times:12:Times:B:distribution of national VAT. This assumption seems to be warranted, given that the VAT tax base is 
11:281:11987:0:18:72:519:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:effectively harmonised between Member States. However, keeping in mind the existing variation of 
11:282:12084:18:18:72:480:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax rates and in national consumption patterns, it must be conceded that incidence patterns 
11:283:12176:18:18:72:516:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:presented here are only indicative. On the other hand, we find a strikingly similar distribution of the 
11:284:12280:18:18:72:421:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:value-added tax burden for Germany, the Netherlands and Spain (table 0.5). 
11:285:12354:18:18:72:75:682:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
11:286:12354:18:21:72:75:664:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
11:287:12354:21:16:72:390:643:12:Times:12:Times:B:Table 0.5  Incidence of new own resource: value added tax (% share)

11:297:12559:18:18:72:518:482:12:Times:12:Times:B:Over the years, various other proposals for new own resources have been fielded. For example, in 
11:298:12656:18:18:72:525:464:12:Times:12:Times:B:the report Stable Money--Sound Finances experts have advanced a tax on `seigniorage', that is the 
11:299:12754:18:18:72:522:446:12:Times:12:Times:B:return for central banks on interest-bearing assets which form the counterpart to the monetary base. 
11:300:12855:18:18:72:491:428:12:Times:12:Times:B:The introduction of this tax would imply that the role of the GNP-based own resource would 
11:301:12946:18:18:72:512:410:12:Times:12:Times:B:commensurately decrease. Given our assumptions, the introduction of a `seigniorage tax' would in 
11:302:13043:18:18:72:465:392:12:Times:12:Times:B:effect not change the present overall incidence of EU own resources (see section 9.2).

15:360:14503:0:18:72:154:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:1    Introduction 
15:361:14520:18:18:72:75:736:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
15:362:14520:18:18:72:524:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:In 1992 total spending of the then European Community (EC) amounted to slightly over ECU 58bn. 
15:363:14615:18:18:72:510:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:The Treaty of Rome forbids the European Union (the former EC) to run deficits. So all outlays of 
15:364:14712:18:18:72:517:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:the Union must be covered by current receipts. In 1992 revenue nearly touched ECU 60bn. Table 
15:365:14806:18:18:72:345:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:1.1 details the composition of the EC budget in 1991-1992.

15:394:15502:17:18:72:75:209:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
15:395:15502:18:18:72:509:191:12:Times:12:Times:B:On the revenue side, the European Union (EU) does not possess fiscal sovereignty, since the EU 
15:396:15597:18:18:72:517:173:12:Times:12:Times:B:budget authority is not empowered to introduce taxes on its own initiative. From 1958 to 1970 the 
15:397:15695:18:18:72:502:155:12:Times:12:Times:B:budget of the former EC was therefore financed by a system of Member State contributions. In 
15:398:15788:18:18:72:497:137:12:Times:12:Times:B:1970 the system of `own resources' was introduced. From then on the present Union is legally 
15:399:15881:18:0:72:204:119:12:Times:12:Times:B:entitled to the revenue from:  
16:400:15912:0:18:72:221:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:(1) agricultural and sugar levies;  
16:401:15947:18:18:72:183:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:(2) customs duties; and  
16:402:15971:18:18:72:519:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:(3) a 1 percent rate on each Member States' value-added tax base. This resource is collected from 
16:403:16069:18:18:72:505:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:the Member States by means of a notional harmonized base, and not as part of value-added tax 
16:404:16162:18:18:72:526:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:(VAT) actually paid by consumers. In 1984 the maximum rate of the VAT resource was raised from 
16:405:16257:18:18:72:490:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:1 to 1.4 percent. In 1989 the tax base itself was capped at 55 percent of the Gross National 
16:406:16350:18:18:72:296:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:Product (GNP) of the Member State concerned. 
16:407:16394:18:18:72:504:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:  As from 1988 the European Union can call on a fourth own resource, on the basis of GNP, to 
16:408:16487:18:18:72:524:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:cover the gap between revenue needed and receipts from the other three own resources mentioned. 
16:409:16582:18:18:72:75:592:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
16:410:16582:18:18:72:478:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:The Edinburgh Summit of December 1992 managed to reach a unanimous position on the 
16:411:16665:18:18:72:510:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:development of the EU budget until 1999. After 1994 the ceiling for own resources will gradually 
16:412:16762:18:18:72:512:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:increase from 1.2 to 1.27 percent of Union GNP. Also, the call-up rate of the VAT-resource will 
16:413:16858:18:18:72:521:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:step-wise be reduced from 1.4 to 1 percent. In addition, the cap on the uniform VAT-base is to be 
16:414:16956:18:18:72:512:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:reduced from the present 55 to 50 percent of GDP. All this implies that the relative importance of 
16:415:17055:18:18:72:356:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:the fourth resource is bound to rise further from 1995 onward. 
16:416:17117:18:18:72:75:466:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
16:417:17117:18:18:72:520:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:Currently, the European Union is actively involved in the search for a fifth own revenue source. The 
16:418:17218:18:18:72:485:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:European Council has explicitly requested the Commission for a report concerning possible 
16:419:17308:18:18:72:238:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:candidates for a fifth own resource.2 
16:420:17345:18:18:72:517:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Recently, a group of independent economists have examined the role of EU public finances in the 
16:421:17443:18:18:72:519:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:perspective of economic and monetary union. These experts have advocated the following changes 
16:422:17538:18:18:72:513:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:on the revenue side of the EU Budget. New own resources should substitute, at least partially, for 
16:423:17637:18:18:72:503:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:the present third and fourth resource, while at least maintaining proportionality, i.e. ensuring that 
16:424:17739:18:18:72:490:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:poorer countries do not pay more and richer ones not less than their respective GDP shares. 
16:425:17831:18:18:72:505:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:European Central Bank profits are advanced as a candidate for new own resources. Other well-
16:426:17923:18:18:72:496:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:suited candidates, in the view of the experts, are a tax on C02 emissions, and corporate taxes. 
16:427:18018:18:18:72:490:268:12:Times:12:Times:B:Qualifying new European taxes can be judged in the light of their contribution to a fair overall 
16:428:18115:18:18:72:513:250:12:Times:12:Times:B:distribution of revenues and expenditures, both within the European Union and among individuals. 
16:429:18212:18:18:72:515:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:One precondition for evaluating both the fairness of the present tax system of Member States, and 
16:430:18310:18:18:72:506:214:12:Times:12:Times:B:to assess proposals for its reform, is adequate knowledge about social and economic impacts of 
16:431:18405:18:18:72:467:196:12:Times:12:Times:B:existing taxes, notably about the distribution of tax burdens within the European Union.  
16:432:18494:18:26:72:340:178:12:Times:12:Times:B:  However, as yet such information is not readily available.  
16:433:18555:26:14:72:219:152:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
16:434:18575:14:13:72:527:138:11:Times:11:Times:F:     2 See Article 10 of the Decision on new own resources by the European Council, dated 31 October 
16:435:18676:13:0:72:475:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:1994 (94/728/EG, Euratom), Journal officiel des Communautés européennes, No L 293/13.  
17:436:18763:0:18:72:75:754:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
17:437:18763:18:18:72:524:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:Recently, the European Commission (DG XIX) has taken initiatives to fill part of existing gaps in our 
17:438:18865:18:18:72:505:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:knowledge of tax incidence in the European Union. As part of that initiative the Commission has 
17:439:18961:18:0:72:361:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:invited the authors of this report to trace "who pays the taxes".   
18:440:19029:0:18:72:246:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:2    Objectives and scope of report 
18:441:19064:18:18:72:75:736:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
18:442:19064:18:18:72:475:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:The European Commission has laid down the following specifications. Our report should: 
18:443:19150:18:18:72:517:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:  a. give a general account of methods and results of empirical analyses of the impact of taxation; 
18:444:19248:18:18:72:308:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:  b. estimate the incidence of national tax systems; 
18:445:19299:18:18:72:304:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:  c. estimate the incidence of each own resource; 
18:446:19347:18:18:72:429:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:  d. estimate the incidence of a limited number of prospective new resources. 
18:447:19423:18:18:72:523:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:The analysis should cover at least three significant Member States. We have decided to include four 
18:448:19523:18:18:72:496:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:Member States, i.e. - in alphabetical order - Germany, the Netherlands, Spain and the United 
18:449:19616:18:18:72:513:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:Kingdom. This selection guarantees the required spread in national "wealth" (measured in terms of 
18:450:19714:18:18:72:527:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:GDP per capita), it covers three "significant" Member States (in terms of both population and GDP), 
18:451:19814:18:18:72:491:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:while sufficient data are available to determine the distribution of tax burdens in each of these 
18:452:19912:18:18:72:122:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:countries.  
18:453:19923:18:18:72:75:520:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
18:454:19923:18:18:72:75:502:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
18:455:19923:18:18:72:177:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:3    Outline of report 
18:456:19945:18:18:72:75:466:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
18:457:19945:18:18:72:509:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:Section 4 briefly outlines the economic profile of the Member States selected for further analysis. 
18:458:20045:18:18:72:522:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:Annex 1 offers a more detailed picture of the economy and the public sector of each Member State 
18:459:20142:18:18:72:506:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:over the 1980-1992 period. For selected Member States, section 5 summarises the national tax 
18:460:20235:18:18:72:328:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:system and revenue trends over the 1980-1992 period.  
18:461:20288:18:18:72:498:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Next, section 6 offers an overview of methods and results of empirical work on the impact of 
18:462:20383:18:18:72:523:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxes. Section 7 offers estimates of the incidence of national tax systems. Annex 2 discusses country 
18:463:20485:18:18:72:496:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:by country the datasets and micromodels that were used to produce these estimates. Annex 3 
18:464:20576:18:18:72:524:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:demonstrates the sensitivity of our results for alternative incidence assumptions. Annex 4 reviews tax 
18:465:20679:18:18:72:242:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:shifting in macroeconometric models. 
18:466:20715:18:18:72:511:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Section 8 presents our estimates of the incidence of each present own resource of the European 
18:467:20812:18:18:72:509:268:12:Times:12:Times:B:Union. The incidence of a limited number of prospective new own resources of the Union will be 
18:468:20907:18:18:72:236:250:12:Times:12:Times:B:taken on in the concluding section.   
18:469:20944:18:0:72:75:232:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
19:470:20945:0:18:72:336:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:4    Country profiles of four selected Member States

19:475:21277:18:21:72:495:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:Germany only). Purchasing power per capita in Spain was at two-thirds of the German level.

20:501:22252:0:18:72:516:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:By the early 1990s all countries ran deficits, because current public receipts fell short of outlays. In 
20:502:22357:18:18:72:516:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:1991, Spain showed the largest gap between public outlays and current receipts. The Netherlands 
20:503:22453:18:18:72:508:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:boasted the smallest deficit, but on the other hand it had the largest public debt in terms of Gross 
20:504:22554:18:18:72:504:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:Domestic Product. However, in just a few years time the debt picture may change dramatically. 
20:505:22648:18:18:72:496:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:According to OECD projections net public debt in the UK and Germany might by 1996 have 
20:506:22735:18:18:72:487:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:swollen to 55 and 58 percent of GDP respectively, whereas the Dutch debt will only slightly 
20:507:22827:18:18:72:516:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:increase to 81 percent of GDP [OECD, 1994, p.29]. Such trends reflect that the Netherlands has 
20:508:22922:18:18:72:410:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:rather successfully tackled its deficit, the recent recession not withstanding. 
20:509:23001:18:18:72:75:610:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
20:510:23001:18:18:72:517:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:Annex 1 offers a more detailed picture of economic trends and public sector developments in each 
20:511:23098:18:18:72:513:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:of the four selected Member States. Broadly speaking, their economies moved in tandem, growth 
20:512:23192:18:18:72:524:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:performance and the public finances reflecting the impact of the deep recession of the first half of the 
20:513:23297:18:18:72:501:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:1980s, the ensuing strong recovery during the second half of the 1980s, followed by the milder 
20:514:23392:18:18:72:208:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:recession of the early 1990s.  
20:515:23422:18:18:72:485:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Over successive cycles, unemployment has risen to an increasingly higher structural level, 
20:516:23515:18:18:72:511:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:presenting policymakers within the EU area with the formidable challenge to create more jobs for 
20:517:23612:18:18:72:296:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:the many millions who are currently out of work.  
20:518:23661:18:18:72:521:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:  During the 1980s the distribution of personal incomes became more unequal, both in the United 
20:519:23757:18:18:72:507:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:Kingdom and the Netherlands. In Spain and Germany, on the other hand, income inequality was 
20:520:23849:18:18:72:315:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:reduced, although in Germany only very modestly so. 
20:521:23900:18:18:72:508:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Between 1980 and 1993 the level of public spending went up strongly in Spain, and increased 
20:522:23994:18:18:72:519:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:somewhat in Germany. The Netherlands and the United Kingdom recorded a slightly lower ratio of 
20:523:24089:18:18:72:518:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:public outlays to GDP. After 1980, the debt-to-GDP ratio rose markedly in three Member States. 
20:524:24184:18:18:72:510:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:Only the United Kingdom substantially cut its public debt as a share of GDP, especially so during 
20:525:24282:18:18:72:218:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:the second half of the 1980s.     
20:526:24315:18:0:72:75:304:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
21:527:24316:0:18:72:318:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:5    Tax systems of four selected Member States 
21:528:24363:18:18:72:75:736:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
21:529:24363:18:18:72:156:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:5.1  Introduction 
21:530:24380:18:18:72:512:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:Ratios of total tax revenue to GDP display much diversity among EU Member States. Moreover, 
21:531:24472:18:18:72:503:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:country positions may strongly vary according to the taxes which are taken into account. This is 
21:532:24569:18:18:72:479:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:especially important as regards the inclusion or the exclusion of compulsory social security 
21:533:24662:18:18:72:509:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:contributions. For example, excluding such contributions, in 1990 the tax level in the Netherlands 
21:534:24761:18:18:72:510:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:was below the EU average. Including social insurance contributions, the Netherlands had and still 
21:535:24859:18:18:72:482:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:has one of the highest tax levels in the whole EU area. This report reckons social insurance 
21:536:24952:18:18:72:178:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:contributions as taxes.  
21:537:24976:18:18:72:75:574:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
21:538:24976:18:18:72:504:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:Table 5.1 shows the ranking of the four EU Member States by their tax-to-GDP ratios. The tax 
21:539:25069:18:18:72:495:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:structure of any country may be characterised by the relative shares of various types of tax. In 
21:540:25166:18:18:72:497:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:addition to total tax levels, table 5.1 displays the tax mix by type of tax for the Member States 
21:541:25264:18:18:72:499:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:considered here. In Germany, the Netherlands and Spain social insurance contributions are the 
21:542:25358:18:18:72:518:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:single most important source of public revenue. In the UK social insurance contributions remain far 
21:543:25458:18:18:72:494:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:behind. Receipts from this source vary strongly among countries, reflecting varying degrees of 
21:544:25553:18:18:72:506:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:coverage and generosity of programmes, as well as different methods of financing social security 
21:545:25650:18:18:72:126:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:transfers.

21:564:26079:14:0:72:75:137:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
22:565:26080:0:18:72:500:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:Only in the Netherlands the share of personal income tax revenues exceeds the EU average. In 
22:566:26173:18:18:72:499:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:Germany the share of the corporate income tax is below average. In relative terms, property is 
22:567:26268:18:18:72:487:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:heavily taxed in the United Kingdom. In Spain, consumption and personal income are taxed 
22:568:26357:18:18:72:174:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:relatively moderately.  
22:569:26380:18:18:72:75:682:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
22:570:26380:18:18:72:141:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:5.2  Germany 
22:571:26392:18:18:72:509:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:Germany finances its public expenditures out of tax revenues on the one hand, and through social 
22:572:26489:18:18:72:496:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:contributions on the other hand. The personal income tax constitutes the single most important 
22:573:26584:18:18:72:494:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:source of public revenue. In the FRG it consists of a wage withholding tax and the income tax 
22:574:26678:18:18:72:506:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:proper. Table 5.2 shows that over the period 1980-1992 the share of the income tax has varied 
22:575:26772:18:18:72:440:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:between 23 and nearly 26 percent of total revenue from taxes and contributions.3 
22:576:26852:18:18:72:522:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Another important tax is the value-added tax (including the import turnover tax) with a tax share of 
22:577:26955:18:18:72:523:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:about 15 percent. The corporate income tax has an average share in the tax mix of about 3 percent. 
22:578:27053:18:18:72:525:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Various duties and consumption taxes, including the mineral oil tax and tobacco taxes, are included 
22:579:27155:18:18:72:496:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:in table 5.2 as `other taxes'. In recent years their share increased from 8 percent (1990) to 10 
22:580:27252:18:18:72:147:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:percent (1992). 
22:581:27267:18:18:72:497:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:With the aim of making the tax system conducive to efficiency and growth, over the past years 
22:582:27361:18:18:72:526:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:numerous changes have been made to tax laws. Examples are the Tax Reduction Act (1986/88) and 
22:583:27455:18:18:72:206:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:the Tax Reform Act (1990).  
22:584:27482:18:18:72:514:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The national social insurance system, which includes old age pensions, health insurance, disability 
22:585:27584:18:18:72:523:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:and unemployment insurance, is financed by both employers and employees. The share of employer 
22:586:27679:18:18:72:507:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:contributions in the tax mix has slightly decreased, to 18.5 percent in 1992, whereas the share of 
22:587:27778:18:18:72:488:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:employee contributions increased from 18 percent (1980) to more than 21 percent (1992).  
22:588:27866:18:18:72:514:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:  It is remarkable, that whereas total revenue from taxes and contributions has doubled after 1980 
22:589:27965:18:18:72:516:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:(from 580bn to 1160bn Dmarks in 1992), the structure of the tax mix has only marginally changed 
22:590:28061:18:21:72:197:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:over the past fifteen years.

23:613:28991:18:18:72:75:585:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
23:614:28991:18:18:72:75:567:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
23:615:28991:18:18:72:155:549:12:Times:12:Times:B:5.3  Netherlands 
23:616:29007:18:18:72:523:531:12:Times:12:Times:B:In the Netherlands, public outlays are over three-quarters financed out of taxes and social insurance 
23:617:29109:18:18:72:489:513:12:Times:12:Times:B:contributions. Non-tax revenues and new debt bridge the gap that remains. In 1992 total tax 
23:618:29201:18:18:72:489:495:12:Times:12:Times:B:revenues amounted to Gld 267bn (table 5.3), which roughly equalled 48 percent of GDP. In 
23:619:29290:18:18:72:511:477:12:Times:12:Times:B:addition to Gld 162bn in central and local government taxes, contributions to finance public social 
23:620:29390:18:18:72:494:459:12:Times:12:Times:B:insurance programmes constitute a very important source of revenue to the public sector (Gld 
23:621:29483:18:18:72:111:441:12:Times:12:Times:B:105bn). 
23:622:29490:18:18:72:525:423:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The personal income tax and contributions to finance the general social insurances dominate the tax 
23:623:29592:18:18:72:526:405:12:Times:12:Times:B:system, each accounting for about one-quarter of total tax revenues. Less than 10 percent of income 
23:624:29692:18:18:72:515:387:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax due is collected by assessment, the remainder being collected by withholding the tax at source, 
23:625:29792:18:18:72:505:369:12:Times:12:Times:B:the latter method being applied to wages, private pensions, social insurance and welfare benefits 
23:626:29890:18:18:72:490:351:12:Times:12:Times:B:(wage tax), and dividends (dividend tax). Resident tax-payers are taxed on their world-wide 
23:627:29982:18:18:72:509:333:12:Times:12:Times:B:income, that has been earned within a given calendar year. As a rule, private capital gains are not 
23:628:30082:18:18:72:511:315:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxed. Income is taxed under a three-bracket rate schedule at 13%, 50% and 60%, respectively. 
23:629:30175:18:18:72:524:297:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In 1991, contributions to finance general social insurances produced nearly Gld 63bn. All residents 
23:630:30277:18:18:72:524:279:12:Times:12:Times:B:are covered by four general social insurance programmes, the most important one being the general 
23:631:30375:18:18:72:496:261:12:Times:12:Times:B:old-age pension scheme. Contributions to finance the general social insurances have a flat rate 
23:632:30471:18:18:72:511:243:12:Times:12:Times:B:(25%), with a cap, since these taxes are due on income in the first income tax bracket only, while 
23:633:30570:18:18:72:502:225:12:Times:12:Times:B:the personal exemptions apply. Thus, the combined rate of the personal income tax and general 
23:634:30664:18:18:72:458:207:12:Times:12:Times:B:social insurance contributions comes to (13+25=) 38%, 50% and 60% respectively.  
23:635:30744:18:18:72:526:189:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Households with a net worth over (roughly) Gld 200,000 are liable to a net wealth tax (rate 0.8%). 
23:636:30845:18:18:72:326:171:12:Times:12:Times:B:Revenues from this net wealth tax amount to Gld 1.4bn. 
23:637:30899:18:18:72:516:153:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Value-added tax and contributions to finance the employee social insurances each raise over Gld 
23:638:30997:18:18:72:503:135:12:Times:12:Times:B:40bn. Participation in the employee social insurances is mandatory for all workers in the market 
23:639:31094:18:0:72:507:117:12:Times:12:Times:B:sector. Insured workers are entitled to benefits in case of unemployment, sickness and disability. 
24:640:31195:0:18:72:492:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:The tax basis is gross wage. Part of this flat rate tax is withheld from employee wages, part is 
24:641:31292:18:18:72:522:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:directly paid by employers. The maximum amount of earnings subject to contributions for employee 
24:642:31389:18:18:72:282:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:social insurances is about Gld 75,000 (1992). 
24:643:31432:18:18:72:507:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In 1992, the corporation income tax produced over Gld 17bn in revenue. Under Dutch tax law 
24:644:31525:18:18:72:465:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:corporate income is taxed both at the level of the company as well as at the level of the 
24:645:31615:18:18:72:504:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:shareholders. As from 1988 the tax rate (which stood at 46% at the end of the 1970s) is 35%.  
24:646:31708:18:18:72:382:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Other central and local government taxes will not be detailed here.  
24:647:31778:18:18:72:75:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:

24:668:32431:17:18:72:75:296:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
24:669:32431:18:18:72:516:278:12:Times:12:Times:B:Over the whole 1980-1992 period, the tax mix in the Netherlands has not fundamentally changed. 
24:670:32526:18:18:72:503:260:12:Times:12:Times:B:However, the share of the personal income tax and employee social insurance contributions has 
24:671:32620:18:18:72:489:242:12:Times:12:Times:B:somewhat declined by -1.6 and -2.3 points respectively, whereas the share of general social 
24:672:32712:18:18:72:507:224:12:Times:12:Times:B:insurance contributions and local plus green taxes increased by 2.2 and 1.5 points respectively.   
24:673:32810:18:18:72:75:206:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
24:674:32810:18:18:72:123:188:12:Times:12:Times:B:5.4  Spain 
24:675:32820:18:18:72:511:170:12:Times:12:Times:B:The present Spanish tax system has its origin in the Tax Reform of 1977 which introduced for the 
24:676:32917:18:18:72:520:152:12:Times:12:Times:B:first time a veritable personal income tax, together with a net wealth tax. The present top rate of the 
24:677:33021:18:18:72:510:134:12:Times:12:Times:B:income tax is 56%. Up till now, the wealth tax has not been very effective in reducing the share in 
24:678:33121:18:0:72:289:116:12:Times:12:Times:B:national income of the most affluent individuals.  
25:679:33173:0:18:72:503:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The corporation income tax was reformed in 1978. It has a flat rate of 35%. Presently, the tax 
25:680:33270:18:18:72:380:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:base is eroded by a wide variety of tax allowances and deductions.  
25:681:33337:18:18:72:516:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The taxation of goods and services underwent important changes in the wake of the 1986 reform 
25:682:33432:18:18:72:515:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:of most indirect taxes, which was motivated by the entry of Spain into the former EC. Particularly, 
25:683:33532:18:18:72:484:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:the introduction of the value-added tax should be mentioned. The share of import taxes has 
25:684:33623:18:18:72:450:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:dramatically dropped, also as a consequence of Spain joining the European Union.  
25:685:33704:18:21:72:75:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:

25:704:34303:16:19:72:75:353:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
25:705:34303:19:17:72:264:334:10:Times:12:Times:B:Source: Banco de España (National Accounts)  
25:706:34347:17:18:72:75:317:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
25:707:34347:18:18:72:512:299:12:Times:12:Times:B:In Spain, social insurance contributions are the single most important revenue source of the public 
25:708:34447:18:18:72:525:281:12:Times:12:Times:B:sector. By 1980, proceeds from such contributions accounted for nearly half of total public revenue. 
25:709:34548:18:18:72:518:263:12:Times:12:Times:B:The share of contributions in the tax mix fell during the first half of the 1980s and remained more or 
25:710:34651:18:18:72:506:245:12:Times:12:Times:B:less stable as from the mid 1980s. Still, social insurance contributions made up over one-third of 
25:711:34750:18:18:72:487:227:12:Times:12:Times:B:total tax revenue in 1992. The second most important tax source is the personal income tax, 
25:712:34842:18:18:72:507:209:12:Times:12:Times:B:producing one-fourth of total revenue in 1992. The share of the personal income tax in GDP has 
25:713:34937:18:18:72:517:191:12:Times:12:Times:B:significantly expanded, as a consequence of progressive rate increases and a marked growth in the 
25:714:35035:18:18:72:524:173:12:Times:12:Times:B:number of persons reporting their income to the tax authorities. Given major changes in the structure 
25:715:35137:18:18:72:527:155:12:Times:12:Times:B:of indirect taxation, the share of taxes on consumption (value-added tax and other indirect taxes) has 
25:716:35240:18:0:72:517:137:12:Times:12:Times:B:remained remarkably stable over the 1980-1992 period, revenue from these sources amounting to 
26:717:35336:0:18:72:508:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:over one-fourth of total tax proceeds. The share of the corporate income tax was rather volatile, 
26:718:35434:18:18:72:196:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:with a clear peak in 1990.  
26:719:35461:18:18:72:75:718:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
26:720:35461:18:18:72:177:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:5.5  United Kingdom 
26:721:35480:18:18:72:516:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:In 1992, UK general government receipts from taxation amounted to £210bn, some 35 percent of 
26:722:35573:18:18:72:479:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:GDP. In terms of revenue raised, the most important UK tax is personal income tax which 
26:723:35661:18:18:72:527:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:generated 27 percent of total tax revenue in 1992. The other major UK taxes are National insurance 
26:724:35760:18:18:72:517:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:(the UK social security tax), value-added tax, corporation income tax and excise duties. Together, 
26:725:35859:18:18:72:357:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:these taxes produce over 80 percent of total UK tax revenues. 
26:726:35920:18:18:72:521:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The income tax has three rates of 20%, 25% and 40%, respectively. Every individual is entitled to 
26:727:36020:18:18:72:523:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:a personal allowance, which varies according to marital status and age. Taxable income greater than 
26:728:36120:18:18:72:508:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:£23,700 is taxed at 40%. For roughly three-quarters of taxpayers, the 25% rate is their marginal 
26:729:36217:18:18:72:502:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:rate of tax. Income tax is levied on an annual basis. The vast majority of revenue is collected by 
26:730:36316:18:18:72:507:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:withholding the tax at source, either by employers or by banks in the case of interest income and 
26:731:36414:18:18:72:192:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:mortgage relief (MIRAS). 
26:732:36438:18:18:72:520:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The UK social security tax, National insurance, is also levied on current income of employees and 
26:733:36538:18:18:72:515:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:the self-employed. National insurance was levied at a rate of 9%, up to a ceiling of £21,840 gross 
26:734:36637:18:18:72:513:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:income in 1993-94. Employers must also pay National insurance with a main contributions rate of 
26:735:36733:18:18:72:518:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:10.4% and no cap. Consequently, the marginal rate faced by most employees in the UK was 34% 
26:736:36825:18:18:72:446:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:in 1993-94, whilst some two million top rate taxpayers faced a 40% marginal rate. 
26:737:36906:18:18:72:519:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Value-added tax was introduced in 1973 when the UK entered the former EC. Since 1991 it has 
26:738:37000:18:18:72:524:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:been levied at a standard rate of 17.5%. Roughly 60 percent of consumer spending is on goods that 
26:739:37098:18:18:72:518:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:fall into the standard rate category, the major exceptions being food, children's clothing, books and 
26:740:37200:18:18:72:517:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:newspapers and transport. Many basic necessities are taxed at zero rates. Excise duties - on beer, 
26:741:37299:18:18:72:505:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:cider, wine, spirits, tobacco, petrol and vehicles - raise significant sums in the UK. In 1992 their 
26:742:37400:18:18:72:348:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:revenue amounted to 70 percent of the proceeds from VAT.
