27:763:38108:16:12:72:75:636:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
27:764:38108:12:12:72:497:624:10:Times:10:Times:F:a) Local personal taxes in 1980 includes business rates, as they were not separately identified for this year. 
27:765:38218:12:12:72:74:612:10:Times:10:Times:F: 
27:766:38218:12:12:72:283:600:10:Times:10:Times:F:Source: Financial Statistics, tables 3.12, 3.13, 3.14 
27:767:38270:12:18:72:395:588:10:Times:10:Times:F:   Financial Statement and Budget Report [1980, 1985, 1990, 1991, 1992] 
27:768:38338:18:18:72:307:570:10:Times:12:Times:B:   Economic Trends Annual Supplement, table 5.4 
27:769:38382:18:18:72:75:552:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
27:770:38382:18:18:72:518:534:12:Times:12:Times:B:Three other taxes raise significant revenues in the UK. Corporation tax, levied on corporate profits 
27:771:38483:18:18:72:501:516:12:Times:12:Times:B:is a combination of a tax on dividend payments (advance corporation tax) which is treated as a 
27:772:38578:18:18:72:520:498:12:Times:12:Times:B:pre-payment of income tax, and a tax on retained profits (mainstream corporation tax), generally at 
27:773:38678:18:18:72:513:480:12:Times:12:Times:B:a rate of 33%. Businesses also have to pay national non-domestic rates, that is, a property tax for 
27:774:38778:18:18:72:506:462:12:Times:12:Times:B:local government services. The council tax is a local property tax and was introduced in 1993 to 
27:775:38875:18:18:72:370:444:12:Times:12:Times:B:replace the community charge, commonly known as the `poll tax'. 
27:776:38938:18:18:72:491:426:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Over the last fifteen years, the UK tax mix has changed substantially, due to both economic 
27:777:39032:18:18:72:491:408:12:Times:12:Times:B:fluctuations and policy changes. The level of profits in the economy accounts for the changing 
27:778:39127:18:18:72:513:390:12:Times:12:Times:B:importance of the corporation tax, while increasing personal incomes over the 1980s kept income 
27:779:39223:18:18:72:504:372:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax revenues very buoyant, despite significant reductions in tax rates in the late 1980s. The most 
27:780:39322:18:18:72:491:354:12:Times:12:Times:B:significant policy change has been the gradually expanding role of the value-added tax, as the 
27:781:39417:18:0:72:388:336:12:Times:12:Times:B:standard rate rose from 8% in 1979 to 17.5% in fiscal year 1993-94. 
28:782:39486:0:18:72:265:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:6    Empirical analysis of tax incidence 
28:783:39526:18:18:72:75:736:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
28:784:39526:18:18:72:156:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:6.1  Introduction 
28:785:39543:18:18:72:527:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:The incidence of a tax is measured by the reduction in real income that results from the imposition of 
28:786:39646:18:18:72:517:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:that tax. Taxes may reduce the income of individuals as producers; or they may increase the prices 
28:787:39745:18:18:72:510:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:of consumer goods and thus reduce the purchasing power of a given money income. Both effects 
28:788:39838:18:18:72:512:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:are measured in this report. However, no attempt is made to measure the burden that results from 
28:789:39935:18:18:72:525:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:the reallocation of resources or the changes in consumption patterns that may be caused by taxation. 
28:790:40035:18:18:72:513:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:  We want to establish who pays the taxes (statutory incidence) and who ultimately bears the tax 
28:791:40132:18:18:72:493:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:burden (economic incidence). Both tax distributions will differ, since individuals and firms are 
28:792:40229:18:18:72:518:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:inclined to shift taxes they must pay onto others. Although some progress has been made in recent 
28:793:40327:18:18:72:506:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:years in improving the methodology of tax analysis, economists still disagree about the economic 
28:794:40424:18:18:72:485:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:incidence of several of the most important taxes in the tax system. Given the state of the art, 
28:795:40520:18:18:72:520:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:estimates of economic incidence will usually be based on a set of incidence assumptions. Once the 
28:796:40618:18:18:72:514:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:statutory incidence of taxes has been established, their economic incidence may be traced under a 
28:797:40716:18:18:72:204:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:variety of such assumptions.  
28:798:40745:18:18:72:509:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:  To measure tax distributions, most economists will start to identify relevant income units, usually 
28:799:40847:18:18:72:525:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:households or families.4 Then, many would prefer to employ a general equilibrium model to calculate 
28:800:40947:18:18:72:518:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:the present value of tax burdens imposed upon each household over its lifetime. This burden would 
28:801:41045:18:18:72:527:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:be compared to the households lifetime income. Recent work of Fullerton and Rogers [1993] stands 
28:802:41142:18:18:72:366:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:as an example of the proper way to implement this methodology. 
28:803:41204:18:18:72:514:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:  However, economists who work in the policy arena usually do not follow this "lifetime approach" 
28:804:41302:18:18:72:518:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:[Barthold, 1993]. Employing various methodologies, government organisations and policy advisors 
28:805:41398:18:18:72:503:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:typically implement some form of "annual approach" [Joint Committee on Taxation, 1993]. This 
28:806:41491:18:18:72:516:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:approach, pioneered by Pechman [1985], estimates the distribution of tax burdens in a given year. 
28:807:41589:18:18:72:494:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:For all kind of practical reasons the annual approach will also be taken in the current research 
28:808:41686:18:18:72:481:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:project, although some economists would maintain the theoretical superiority of the lifetime 
28:809:41779:18:18:72:121:268:12:Times:12:Times:B:approach. 
28:810:41788:18:18:72:75:250:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
28:811:41788:18:18:72:496:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:Sections 6.2 and 6.3 explore the "Pechman approach" in greater detail and specify our shifting 
28:812:41883:18:18:72:483:214:12:Times:12:Times:B:assumptions. Section 6.4 will clarify how these assumptions relate to the shifting of taxes as 
28:813:41978:18:18:72:372:196:12:Times:12:Times:B:embodied in various, frequently used macroeconometric models.   
28:814:42041:18:18:72:75:178:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
28:815:42041:18:22:72:231:160:12:Times:12:Times:B:6.2  Statutory incidence of taxes 
28:816:42074:22:13:72:219:138:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
28:817:42094:13:0:72:367:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:     4 Household definitions may vary from one country to another.  
29:818:42163:0:18:72:500:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:Individuals pay taxes on the income they earn and on benefits received from the public sector.5 
29:819:42258:18:18:72:512:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:When spending their income on goods and services, prices will usually include one or more taxes, 
29:820:42355:18:18:72:487:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:such as value-added tax, excises and import duties. To establish how much tax an individual 
29:821:42447:18:18:72:500:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:household actually pays in income and consumption taxes, any of two roads may be followed.  
29:822:42538:18:18:72:506:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:  First, the necessary data may directly come from government or private administrations. As an 
29:823:42634:18:18:72:514:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:example, the amount of personal income tax paid by households can be taken from the records of 
29:824:42729:18:18:72:524:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:the tax administration. However, in most cases researchers have no access to data from government 
29:825:42827:18:18:72:511:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:administrations. The other route for them to follow is to ask individuals or private firms how much 
29:826:42927:18:18:72:466:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:they pay in specific taxes. As an example, researchers may organise a survey and ask a 
29:827:43014:18:18:72:520:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:representative sample of the population how much they paid in personal income tax or wealth tax in 
29:828:43113:18:18:72:521:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:the previous year. In most cases, however, surveys do not contain explicit questions about amounts 
29:829:43212:18:18:72:468:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:of taxes paid. Moreover, in many cases individuals are not aware how much they pay in 
29:830:43298:18:18:72:506:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:consumption taxes because in Europe, typically, such taxes are not separately identified on sales 
29:831:43396:18:18:72:101:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:slips.  
29:832:43403:18:18:72:522:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Still, given the necessary income and consumption data of households, the amounts paid in income 
29:833:43502:18:18:72:516:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:and consumption taxes can be calculated, using a microanalytic model. Techniques available to 
29:834:43596:18:18:72:504:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:microsimulate tax burdens of individual households are discussed in, among others, Orcutt et al. 
29:835:43693:18:18:72:422:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:(1986), Atkinson and Sutherland (1988), and Brunner and Petersen (1990).  
29:836:43766:18:18:72:489:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Separate modules of such micromodels calculate personal income tax, and social insurance 
29:837:43857:18:18:72:489:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:contributions due, given the income of each household in a representative sample, and taking 
29:838:43950:18:18:72:511:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:account of its relevant socio-economic and demographic household characteristics. For example, 
29:839:44045:18:18:72:521:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:the amount of personal income tax due will - apart from income - also depend on marital status and 
29:840:44144:18:18:72:503:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:may vary with the number of children in the household. Also, provided the data set contains the 
29:841:44240:18:18:72:512:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:relevant information, deductions and exempted income can be taken into account in simulating the 
29:842:44337:18:18:72:520:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:amount of income tax due. If social insurance contributions are deductible for income tax purposes, 
29:843:44437:18:18:72:512:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:the model first simulates contributions due. Next, this amount is deducted in simulating the income 
29:844:44537:18:18:72:114:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax due.  
29:845:44546:18:18:72:501:268:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Likewise, the burden of value-added tax, excises and import duties can be estimated for each 
29:846:44641:18:18:72:523:250:12:Times:12:Times:B:individual household in a representative sample, by applying relevant tax rates to all items consumed 
29:847:44743:18:18:72:201:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:as known from survey data. 
29:848:44769:18:18:72:415:214:12:Times:12:Times:B:  To summarize, to establish who pays how much in taxes, researchers may: 
29:849:44842:18:18:72:405:196:12:Times:12:Times:B:- take tax amounts as registered in government or private administrations; 
29:850:44916:18:40:72:309:178:12:Times:12:Times:B:- use tax amounts as reported in household surveys; 
29:851:44967:40:13:72:219:138:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
29:852:44987:13:0:72:494:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:     5 It may be noted that Member States tend to exempt certain benefits from income taxation. 
30:853:45084:0:18:72:523:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:- allocate taxes in proportion to other items (for example, dividend income, food consumption) from 
30:854:45184:18:18:72:195:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:administrations or surveys; 
30:855:45211:18:18:72:471:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:- microsimulate tax amounts, using relevant information from administrations or surveys.  
30:856:45300:18:18:72:515:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The final column of tables 7.2 through 7.5, which detail tax incidence in each of the four Member 
30:857:45400:18:18:72:428:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:States, indicates for each tax how its statutory incidence has been established.  
30:858:45481:18:18:72:75:664:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
30:859:45481:18:18:72:511:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:From the foregoing discussion, it follows that the availability of adequate data for a representative 
30:860:45583:18:18:72:371:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:sample of households is essential to establish who pays the taxes.  
30:861:45650:18:18:72:513:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:For each household in the sample the files must contain data on income from various sources, and 
30:862:45747:18:18:72:499:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:also demographic and other economic information, such as the age of household members, the 
30:863:45838:18:18:72:372:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:consumption on goods and services, home ownership, and so on.  
30:864:45900:18:18:72:521:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In case the necessary microdata are not or only partially available in one and the same dataset, tax 
30:865:46003:18:18:72:456:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:researchers may combine data from two or more sources (administrations, surveys).  
30:866:46085:18:18:72:510:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:  If no tax and household data are available from administrations or representative surveys among 
30:867:46183:18:18:72:507:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:the population, tax researchers might also take recourse to an analysis of the tax burden of a few 
30:868:46282:18:18:72:520:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:selected representative economic agents, for example a low, medium and high income household 
30:869:46375:18:18:72:525:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:with given socio-economic and demographic status, and calculate the statutory incidence of personal 
30:870:46475:18:18:72:524:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:income tax and employee social insurance contributions, applying standard tax deductions only. This 
30:871:46575:18:18:72:511:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:approach underlies calculations of the tax/benefit position of production workers that are annually 
30:872:46675:18:18:72:500:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:published by the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development [OECD, 1994a]. 
30:873:46762:18:18:72:496:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:Likewise, the burden of consumption taxes may be estimated by analyzing data - from budget 
30:874:46853:18:18:72:476:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:surveys, and national accounts - for a few consumer households deemed to be sufficiently 
30:875:46942:18:18:72:464:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:representative for the population as a whole. We will not report on tax burdens of such 
30:876:47030:18:18:72:523:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:representative households, because fortunately rich datasets are available which allow to trace taxes 
30:877:47132:18:18:72:523:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:actually paid by a representative sample from the total population. The datasets that have been used 
30:878:47233:18:18:72:183:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:are detailed in Annex 2. 
30:879:47257:18:18:72:75:286:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
30:880:47257:18:18:72:234:268:12:Times:12:Times:B:6.3  Economic incidence of taxes 
30:881:47289:18:18:72:515:250:12:Times:12:Times:B:We have already remarked that in order to determine who bears the tax burden, it is necessary to 
30:882:47386:18:18:72:520:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:consider how different taxes may be shifted from some individuals onto others. Studies which try to 
30:883:47486:18:18:72:520:214:12:Times:12:Times:B:trace the economic incidence of taxes by income class must include a set of assumptions about the 
30:884:47584:18:18:72:491:196:12:Times:12:Times:B:incidence of major taxes. Following Pechman [1985, Ch. 3] we have selected a set of rather 
30:885:47675:18:18:72:516:178:12:Times:12:Times:B:eclectic incidence assumptions which underpin the results to be presented in chapters 7 through 9:  
30:886:47774:18:18:72:512:160:12:Times:12:Times:B:A. Personal income tax (including wage tax) and net wealth tax are assumed not to be shifted and 
30:887:47871:18:0:72:279:142:12:Times:12:Times:B:are thus borne by those who pay these taxes. 
31:888:47917:0:18:72:505:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:B. Value-added tax, excises, import duties, agricultural levies and the car tax are assumed to be 
31:889:48015:18:18:72:508:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:borne by consumers of the taxed commodities in proportion to their consumption of taxed items. 
31:890:48109:18:18:72:486:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:C. Social insurance contributions paid by workers, self-employed and benefit recipients are 
31:891:48201:18:18:72:212:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:assumed to be borne by them. 
31:892:48229:18:18:72:488:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:D. Social insurance contributions imposed on employers are assumed to be shifted for three-
31:893:48320:18:18:72:342:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:quarters to employees, and for one-quarter to consumers.   
31:894:48378:18:18:72:510:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:E. Corporation income tax (plus dividend tax) is allocated one-third to shareholders, one-third to 
31:895:48477:18:18:72:325:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:property income in general and one-third to consumers. 
31:896:48531:18:18:72:510:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:F. Property tax on commercial and industrial buildings is assumed to be shifted to consumers; the 
31:897:48629:18:18:72:434:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:property tax on houses is borne by renters and owner-occupiers respectively.6   
31:898:48708:18:18:72:75:574:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
31:899:48708:18:18:72:522:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:Results presented in our report of course critically depend on this set of assumptions. However, our 
31:900:48809:18:18:72:502:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:results do not change very much if alternative plausible sets of assumptions are adopted. This is 
31:901:48907:18:18:72:526:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:explained because in the relevant literature the incidence of major taxes seems to be in little doubt. In 
31:902:49013:18:18:72:520:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:his pathbreaking study, Pechman (1985, p.35) used nine separate sets of incidence assumptions. In 
31:903:49111:18:18:72:494:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:each case, however, assumptions A, B and C were taken to apply. Pechman used alternative 
31:904:49200:18:18:72:513:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:assumptions to trace the economic incidence of corporation income tax, property taxes and social 
31:905:49297:18:18:72:490:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:insurance contributions levied from employers. Because these taxes have no dominant role in 
31:906:49389:18:18:72:480:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:national tax mixes, it follows that the combined incidence of all taxes changes rather little, if 
31:907:49487:18:18:72:462:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:alternative shifting assumptions are adopted. This conclusion is illustrated in Annex 3.   
31:908:49577:18:18:72:75:394:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
31:909:49577:18:18:72:499:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:Our incidence assumptions may also be compared to the shifting of taxes which is embodied in 
31:910:49670:18:18:72:510:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:`behavioural equations' that are part of widely used macroeconometric models. There are a great 
31:911:49766:18:18:72:526:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:many of such models, which are typically employed to analyse the short and medium term impacts of 
31:912:49864:18:18:72:500:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:various policy measures, including effects of changes in tax rates. However, macroeconometric 
31:913:49958:18:18:72:509:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:models are less suited to estimate the long term economic incidence of taxes, which is exactly the 
31:914:50057:18:26:72:522:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:topic of our paper. Annex 4 surveys tax shifting in prominent macroeconometric models presently in 
31:915:50156:26:14:72:219:260:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
31:916:50176:14:13:72:527:246:11:Times:11:Times:F:     6 As to assumption C, it might be remarked that as employer social insurance contributions increase 
31:917:50281:13:14:72:526:233:11:Times:11:Times:F:the  gap  between  the  producer  price  and  the  consumer  price  of  labour,  they  are  not  different  in 
31:918:50392:14:13:72:527:219:11:Times:11:Times:F:incidence  from  employee  social  insurance  contributions.  Hence,  it  might  alternatively  be  assumed  that  
31:919:50507:13:14:72:373:206:11:Times:11:Times:F:the burden would fully be shifted to employees, and not for only 3/4. 
31:920:50576:14:13:72:526:192:11:Times:11:Times:F:As  to  assumptions  D  (and  E)  the  following  observation  seems  to  be  in  order.  Given  efficient  capital  
31:921:50693:13:14:72:526:179:11:Times:11:Times:F:markets,  share  prices  will  change  so  as  to  equalise  rates  of  return  taking  into  account  existing 
31:922:50805:14:13:72:526:165:11:Times:11:Times:F:corporate  tax  regimes.  For  this  reason,  corporate  taxes  are  not  only  paid  by  shareholders.  It  is  most  
31:923:50924:13:14:72:526:152:11:Times:11:Times:F:likely, that instead corporate taxes are borne in part by consumers and labour, the exact mix depending 
31:924:51028:14:13:72:527:138:11:Times:11:Times:F:partly on the proportion of products that is exported. However, the incidence assumptions chosen here 
31:925:51130:13:0:72:329:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:more closely reflect an `average' of Pechman's approach. 
32:926:51188:0:18:72:521:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:use in the four Member States. It appears that the specification of these models is very different. As 
32:927:51291:18:18:72:525:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:a consequence, the effects of a shift in e.g. the VAT-rate by one point are not uniformly available for 
32:928:51395:18:18:72:237:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:the countries included in this paper.  
32:929:51433:18:18:72:526:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Also, macroeconometric models do not cover the effects (and so the incidence) of changes in most 
32:930:51532:18:18:72:503:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:smaller taxes on income, capital and consumption. For all of these reasons, macromodels are of 
32:931:51627:18:18:72:503:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:limited help if one tries to assess the value of the shifting assumptions adopted in our paper. For 
32:932:51727:18:18:72:509:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:good measure, section 6.4 discusses tax incidence in macroeconometric models in greater detail. 
32:933:51822:18:18:72:75:628:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
32:934:51822:18:18:72:305:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:6.4  Tax incidence in macroeconometric models 
32:935:51867:18:18:72:75:592:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
32:936:51867:18:18:72:233:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:6.4.1. Macroeconometric models 
32:937:51897:18:18:72:523:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:Economic forecasters and policy analysts often rely on economic models. Such models describe the 
32:938:51994:18:18:72:481:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:economy, generally at the national level. Using historical data, models give a consistent and 
32:939:52088:18:18:72:482:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:comprehensive account of relevant interactions and interdependencies within the economy. 
32:940:52177:18:18:72:524:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:Variables that are explained within the model are called `endogenous', whereas exogenous variables 
32:941:52276:18:18:72:519:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:are given, i.e. they are input for the model and affect its outcomes, but they are not explained within 
32:942:52380:18:18:72:126:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:the model.  
32:943:52391:18:18:72:513:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Nowadays, macroeconometric models often contain hundreds of equations. Some are so-called 
32:944:52483:18:18:72:515:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:`behavioural equations', which try to capture behaviour of economic agents, like consumers, firms, 
32:945:52582:18:18:72:501:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:etcetera. Such behavioural equations are pivotal to understand the nature of macroeconometric 
32:946:52676:18:18:72:237:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:models, as will shortly be explained. 
32:947:52713:18:18:72:491:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Standard policy analysis with macroeconometric models includes "what-if" exercises. Here, 
32:948:52805:18:18:72:515:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:analysts address the question what would be the economic consequences if present policies were 
32:949:52900:18:18:72:509:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:changed. The answer is obtained by comparing the results of two simulation runs with the model. 
32:950:52996:18:18:72:520:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:The first run produces a so-called baseline simulation, which could refer to a future forecast period, 
32:951:53099:18:18:72:502:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:whereas in the second simulation the model is re-run over the same period, but now with policy 
32:952:53194:18:18:72:523:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:variables deemed relevant given their new values. The baseline scenario is typically a forecast with a 
32:953:53297:18:18:72:492:268:12:Times:12:Times:B:`no-change' or `neutral' policy stance. The difference between the two simulation runs for the 
32:954:53392:18:18:72:497:250:12:Times:12:Times:B:endogenous variables provides an assessment of potential effects of the policy under scrutiny.  
32:955:53487:18:18:72:499:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Standard what-if exercises remain limited to studying the effects of policy instruments that are 
32:956:53586:18:18:72:520:214:12:Times:12:Times:B:included in the original specification of the model. The effects of raising value-added tax rates might 
32:957:53690:18:18:72:502:196:12:Times:12:Times:B:for example be simulated with a macroeconometric model. This implies that certain other policy 
32:958:53785:18:18:72:500:178:12:Times:12:Times:B:proposals, like the introduction of a new tax, for instance a tax on emissions of carbon dioxide, 
32:959:53883:18:18:72:495:160:12:Times:12:Times:B:cannot be properly evaluated with these models. The same applies for the introduction of new 
32:960:53976:18:18:72:511:142:12:Times:12:Times:B:institutional arrangements. General equilibrium models (subsection 6.4.2) are better suited for this 
32:961:54077:18:0:72:153:124:12:Times:12:Times:B:type of analysis.   
33:962:54098:0:18:72:75:754:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
33:963:54098:18:18:72:509:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:Macroeconometric models typically analyze the short and medium term impacts of various policy 
33:964:54192:18:18:72:520:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:measures, including effects of changes in tax rates. Their value to determine the economic incidence 
33:965:54293:18:18:72:518:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:of taxes in the long run is thus subject to limitations, for example because many of these models are 
33:966:54395:18:18:72:251:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:not stable over long simulation periods. 
33:967:54435:18:18:72:514:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Still, it may be useful to compare our incidence assumptions (as set out in section 7.1) with those 
33:968:54537:18:18:72:512:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:included in macroeconometric models. After reviewing some trends in modelbuilding we will - for 
33:969:54633:18:18:72:354:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:reasons to be explained - focus upon the modelling of wages.  
33:970:54694:18:18:72:75:610:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
33:971:54694:18:18:72:225:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:6.4.2  Trends in model building 
33:972:54725:18:18:72:511:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:Different models are built for different purposes, and both models and the problems they address 
33:973:54822:18:18:72:469:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:evolve over time. New statistical evidence will sometimes change perceptions of existing 
33:974:54911:18:18:72:502:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:relationships, and social and political changes may alter the focus of economic attention [Wallis, 
33:975:55010:18:18:72:513:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:1993]. Looking at the period 1960-1985, Bodkin [1988] found various trends. Initially, the trend 
33:976:55107:18:18:72:292:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:was an evolution towards large scale modelling.  
33:977:55155:18:18:72:523:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Macroeconometric models grew bigger and bigger, which made their outcomes sometimes hard to 
33:978:55249:18:18:72:501:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:interpret. A second trend to be discerned was the increasing theoretical sophistication of model 
33:979:55346:18:18:72:508:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:building. Developments in macroeconomic theory tend to be incorporated into the models, albeit 
33:980:55441:18:18:72:520:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:generally only after some time has passed. A final trend has been the increased orientation of model 
33:981:55542:18:18:72:511:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:builders towards policy issues. However, it became increasingly clear that not all policy questions 
33:982:55642:18:18:72:294:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:could be properly addressed by existing models. 
33:983:55689:18:18:72:526:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:  During the 1980s, at many academic research centers interest in macroeconometric models waned. 
33:984:55786:18:18:72:527:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:Nevertheless, such models are still widely used for policy analysis, both by national governments and 
33:985:55888:18:18:72:507:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:by international organisations like the OECD. Wallis [1993] has pointed out that the supply side 
33:986:55984:18:18:72:514:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:became the catch-phrase of the 1980s. The previous macroeconomic paradigm over-emphasized 
33:987:56074:18:18:72:521:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:effective demand, and had proved inadequate to deal with the supply-side shocks of the 1970s. As 
33:988:56171:18:18:72:518:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:a consequence, macroeconometric modellers now showed greater interest in the supply side of the 
33:989:56267:18:18:72:126:268:12:Times:12:Times:B:economy.   
33:990:56277:18:18:72:490:250:12:Times:12:Times:B:  A recent, very important development is the construction of so-called general equilibrium 
33:991:56369:18:18:72:477:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:models. The aim of applied general equilibrium modelling is to transform abstract classical 
33:992:56461:18:18:72:505:214:12:Times:12:Times:B:equilibrium models into realistic representations of actual economies and to use these models for 
33:993:56559:18:18:72:515:196:12:Times:12:Times:B:policy analysis [Kehoe et al., 1988; Gelauff and Graafland, 1994]. An important advantage of this 
33:994:56657:18:18:72:526:178:12:Times:12:Times:B:type of models is their solid theoretical foundation. The behaviour of economic agents in the model is 
33:995:56760:18:18:72:526:160:12:Times:12:Times:B:based upon optimisation principles. Applied general equilibrium models are well suited to analyze the 
33:996:56862:18:18:72:499:142:12:Times:12:Times:B:economic and welfare consequences of (changes in) the tax system. Such models are generally 
33:997:56954:18:0:72:502:124:12:Times:12:Times:B:calibrated, which means that relevant elasticities are taken from the economic literature and that 
34:998:57055:0:18:72:526:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:other parameters are computed in such a way as to match the base year solution of the model with a 
34:999:57154:18:18:72:164:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:benchmark dataset. 
34:1000:57172:18:18:72:511:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:Annex 4 reviews econometric models of the Dutch7 and the UK economy8; also the model of the 
34:1001:57264:18:18:72:428:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:Deutsche Bundesbank and the Spanish MOISEES model are presented here.  
34:1002:57334:18:18:72:75:682:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
34:1003:57334:18:18:72:197:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:6.4.3  The wage equation 
34:1004:57358:18:18:72:515:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:Indirect taxes raise the price level. Wage tax and social insurance contributions eat into net wages. 
34:1005:57460:18:18:72:524:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:In response, workers will try to shift indirect and direct taxes by claiming higher nominal wages. This 
34:1006:57564:18:18:72:475:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:subsection discusses how the process of wage formation and tax shifting is represented in 
34:1007:57654:18:18:72:506:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:macroeconometric models. Usually, macromodels have no comparable equations describing the 
34:1008:57744:18:18:72:523:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:behaviour of economic agents which supply capital. For this reason, our discussion will be limited to 
34:1009:57846:18:18:72:496:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:the wage equation. Results are summarised here, so as to allow a comparison with our shifting 
34:1010:57940:18:18:72:196:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:assumptions (section 6.3).  
34:1011:57967:18:18:72:520:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The most commonly adopted approach in current models of the German, Dutch, Spanish and UK 
34:1012:58059:18:18:72:526:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:economies assumes that firms and unions bargain over wages, and that employment is determined by 
34:1013:58156:18:18:72:501:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:firms. Wage negotiations typically focus on the level of nominal wages. This does not mean that 
34:1014:58252:18:18:72:503:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:employers and employees are insensitive to inflation, but rather that different wage concepts are 
34:1015:58350:18:18:72:506:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:relevant to their objectives [Wallis, 1993]. What matters for employers are real wage costs, i.e. 
34:1016:58448:18:18:72:526:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:nominal wages plus employers' taxes deflated by producer prices, whereas employees focus on their 
34:1017:58546:18:18:72:480:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:real consumption wage, i.e. nominal wages less direct taxes deflated by consumer prices.  
34:1018:58635:18:18:72:513:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The wedge is defined as the gap between real labour costs of the firm, on the one hand, and real 
34:1019:58734:18:18:72:521:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:disposable income of workers on the other [Layard et al., 1991]. The building blocks of the wedge 
34:1020:58832:18:18:72:518:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:thus consists of the tax rates applying to both employers and employees and the price of consumer 
34:1021:58930:18:18:72:211:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:goods relative to value added. 
34:1022:58960:18:18:72:493:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The way the wedge variable is included in macroeconometric models has different incidence 
34:1023:59052:18:18:72:502:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:implications. From our analysis of tax shifting behaviour as embodied in wage equations in large 
34:1024:59149:18:14:72:519:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:macroeconometric models the following conclusion can be drawn. There is clearly no consensus as 
34:1025:59245:14:14:72:219:272:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
34:1026:59265:14:13:72:526:258:11:Times:11:Times:F:     7  The  Netherlands  have  a  long  tradition  in  econometric  modelbuilding  (see  Barten  [1988]  and  
34:1027:59376:13:14:72:526:245:11:Times:11:Times:F:Bodkin  et  al.  [1991]  for  reviews).  Starting  with  the  work  of  Jan  Tinbergen,  the  Central  Planning 
34:1028:59488:14:13:72:527:231:11:Times:11:Times:F:Bureau (CPB) has developed and used various macroeconometric models of the Dutch economy. The 
34:1029:59582:13:14:72:526:218:11:Times:11:Times:F:model  presently  in  use  (FKSEC)  is  quite  eclectic  in  the  sense  that  the  supply  side  of  the  economy  
34:1030:59698:14:13:72:527:204:11:Times:11:Times:F:consists  of  a  vintage  model,  whereas  the  demand  side  has  certain  Keynesian  features.  FKSEC  is  
34:1031:59807:13:14:72:526:191:11:Times:11:Times:F:mainly  used  for  short-term  analyses.  More  recently,  CPB  has  started  work  on  general  equilibrium  
34:1032:59917:14:13:72:524:177:11:Times:11:Times:F:models.  The  MIMIC  model  is  such  a  model  which  is  presently  in  use,  especially  to  analyze  the  long-
34:1033:60032:13:26:72:238:164:11:Times:11:Times:F:term effects of welfare state reform. 
34:1034:60069:26:13:72:526:138:11:Times:11:Times:F:     8 Reviews of UK econometric models are provided by Bodkin et al. [1991], Fisher et al. [1990] and 
34:1035:60172:13:0:72:193:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:Church et al. [1991, 1993]. 
35:1036:60201:0:18:72:508:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:to the degree labour is able - in the short to medium run - to shift forward higher wage taxes and 
35:1037:60300:18:18:72:516:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:social insurance contributions. Most models conclude that there is at least some forward shifting of 
35:1038:60401:18:18:72:247:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:such taxes, but estimates vary widely.  
35:1039:60440:18:18:72:503:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Still, most models seem to agree that tax shifting is far from complete. However, some authors 
35:1040:60537:18:18:72:496:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:present evidence that elements of the wedge have a large and permanent effect on wages. For 
35:1041:60629:18:18:72:524:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:instance, Knoester and Van der Windt [1987] find that employee taxes have a permanent impact on 
35:1042:60725:18:18:72:519:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:wages in ten OECD countries. However, the coefficients found by these authors are extremely high 
35:1043:60822:18:18:72:512:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:and are out of line with most other available evidence. Cross-section evidence reported in OECD 
35:1044:60918:18:18:72:422:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:[1990, Annex 6A] indicates that short-run wedge effects are very important.  
35:1045:60994:18:18:72:518:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:  On average, for sixteen OECD countries, a 1 percent rise in the wedge induces an immediate rise 
35:1046:61092:18:18:72:490:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:in labour costs of 0.5 percent. Even after five years, nearly half this effect remains. However, 
35:1047:61189:18:18:72:506:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:according to the same OECD study, in the long run increases of the wedge are entirely borne by 
35:1048:61284:18:0:72:318:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:labour, in line with our assumptions here (section 6.3). 
36:1049:61342:0:18:72:259:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:7    Incidence of national tax systems 
36:1050:61380:18:18:72:75:736:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
36:1051:61380:18:18:72:156:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:7.1  Introduction 
36:1052:61397:18:18:72:501:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:This section estimates and discusses distributions of statutory and economic tax burdens in four 
36:1053:61494:18:18:72:511:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:selected Member States of the European Union. Tax incidence will be estimated for some year in 
36:1054:61589:18:18:72:497:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:the early 1990s, using recent microdata for representative samples of households. It should be 
36:1055:61684:18:18:72:463:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:stressed that only this micro approach allows distributional analyses as presented here. 
36:1056:61772:18:18:72:517:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Given the limitations inherent to available microdata, it was not possible to calculate the burden of 
36:1057:61876:18:18:72:520:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:all taxes. Taxes covered in this report range from between 62 percent of total taxes for Germany to 
36:1058:61976:18:18:72:512:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:98 percent of all taxes for the Netherlands (table 7.1). Also, the base year is not exactly the same 
36:1059:62077:18:18:72:522:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:for countries included in our analysis. Given the small spread in the base year (1989-1993)9 and the 
36:1060:62178:18:18:72:496:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:generally observed relative stability of tax structures and income distributions over limited time 
36:1061:62277:18:18:72:510:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:periods, results presented here still allow comparison of the distribution of tax burdens in the four 
36:1062:62379:18:18:72:523:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:EU Member States under consideration. The surveys that have been used are detailed in Annex 2.   
36:1063:62475:18:21:72:75:502:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
36:1064:62475:21:16:72:278:481:12:Times:12:Times:B:Table 7.1  Taxes covered and datasets used  
36:1065:62518:16:15:72:75:465:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
36:1066:62518:15:15:72:527:450:12:Times:12:Times:B:     taxes covered (%)     dataset     year 
36:1067:62546:15:15:72:75:435:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
36:1068:62546:15:15:72:527:420:12:Times:12:Times:B:Germany       62     GSOEP          1990 
36:1069:62564:15:15:72:527:405:12:Times:12:Times:B:                EVS           1983 
36:1070:62571:15:15:72:527:390:12:Times:12:Times:B:Netherlands      98     Panel Survey of Income    1991 
36:1071:62610:15:15:72:527:375:12:Times:12:Times:B:                Consumer Survey      1992 
36:1072:62629:15:15:72:527:360:12:Times:12:Times:B:                Housing Demand Survey    1989 
36:1073:62654:15:15:72:527:345:12:Times:12:Times:B:Spain        93     Family Expenditure Survey   1990 
36:1074:62690:15:19:72:527:330:12:Times:12:Times:B:United Kingdom    94     Family Expenditure Survey   1993 
36:1075:62735:19:18:72:75:311:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
36:1076:62735:18:18:72:524:293:12:Times:12:Times:B:To calculate tax distributions, a four-step procedure will be followed. First, for each country one or 
36:1077:62838:18:18:72:505:275:12:Times:12:Times:B:more representative samples with household data have been selected. In their characteristics the 
36:1078:62935:18:18:72:478:257:12:Times:12:Times:B:households in these samples closely mirror the population at large. Second, the taxes each 
36:1079:63026:18:18:72:506:239:12:Times:12:Times:B:household in the sample pays have to be determined. It will be recalled from section 6.2 that the 
36:1080:63124:18:18:72:526:221:12:Times:12:Times:B:amount of taxes households pay may be traced in either of three ways. Sometimes information about 
36:1081:63222:18:18:72:522:203:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxes paid is directly available in the dataset (from an administration or survey). In other cases taxes 
36:1082:63327:18:47:72:511:185:12:Times:12:Times:B:paid have been simulated, for example by combining consumption data and statutory VAT-rates. 
36:1083:63420:47:13:72:219:138:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
36:1084:63440:13:0:72:305:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:     9 The German EVS (1983) is the exception here. 
37:1085:63493:0:18:72:506:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:Also, given income components and household composition, levies on income may be simulated 
37:1086:63584:18:18:72:198:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:with a microanalytic model. 
37:1087:63611:18:18:72:515:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The final column of tables 7.2 through 7.5, which detail tax incidence in each of the four Member 
37:1088:63711:18:18:72:474:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:States, contains a code, which indicates for each tax how its statutory incidence has been 
37:1089:63802:18:18:72:127:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:established: 
37:1090:63814:18:18:72:438:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:ADM - tax amount as registered in government or private administrations; or 
37:1091:63887:18:18:72:522:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:   - taxes allocated in proportion to other items from administrations (for example, dividend 
37:1092:63977:18:18:128:170:628:12:Times:12:Times:A:income); 
37:1093:63985:18:18:72:333:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:SUR - tax amount as reported in household surveys; or 
37:1094:64036:18:18:72:472:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:   - taxes allocated in proportion to other items from surveys (for example, food 
37:1095:64114:18:18:128:195:574:12:Times:12:Times:A:consumption); 
37:1096:64127:18:18:72:495:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:SIM  - tax amount has been simulated, using relevant information from administrations or 
37:1097:64213:18:18:128:171:538:12:Times:12:Times:A:surveys.  
37:1098:64222:18:18:72:75:520:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
37:1099:64222:18:18:72:497:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:Once taxes paid by each household have been determined, as a third step, all households are 
37:1100:64314:18:18:72:523:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:ranked in ten 10-percent groups - commonly called `deciles' - by increasing income. The first decile 
37:1101:64415:18:18:72:495:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:contains the ten percent of households with lowest incomes, the tenth decile comprises the ten 
37:1102:64510:18:18:72:276:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:percent of households with highest incomes.  
37:1103:64554:18:18:72:522:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In the fourth step, the share of (households in) each decile in the total revenue from each separate 
37:1104:64657:18:18:72:479:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax is established. The combined economic incidence of all taxes is then found by weighing 
37:1105:64748:18:18:72:454:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:distributions of individual taxes over deciles by their share in total revenue collected.  
37:1106:64838:18:18:72:511:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Apart from potential weaknesses embodied in our shifting assumptions, a further caveat applies. 
37:1107:64936:18:18:72:526:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:For technical reasons the crucial concepts of `household' and `income' may differ between countries. 
37:1108:65037:18:18:72:472:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:Such differences and their potential consequences are more fully examined in Annex 2A. 
37:1109:65123:18:18:72:75:322:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
37:1110:65123:18:18:72:141:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:7.2  Germany 
37:1111:65135:18:18:72:524:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:Table 7.2 shows the economic incidence of 62 percent of all taxes levied in Germany (distribution of 
37:1112:65236:18:18:72:514:268:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax shares by decile). The results obtained are based on survey data for 1983 (value-added tax)10 
37:1113:65333:18:18:72:525:250:12:Times:12:Times:B:and for 1990 (all other taxes). Given available data, the incidence of only three major taxes could be 
37:1114:65436:18:18:72:526:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:traced: the personal income tax, value-added tax and employee social insurance contributions. Given 
37:1115:65536:18:18:72:515:214:12:Times:12:Times:B:the three taxes included in the analysis and the composition of the German tax mix vis-à-vis the tax 
37:1116:65637:18:18:72:526:196:12:Times:12:Times:B:mix of the other three Member States, there is no reason to expect a priori a fundamentally different 
37:1117:65739:18:26:72:513:178:12:Times:12:Times:B:pattern of tax incidence between all countries considered in this report. Moreover, customs duties

40:1168:68332:18:18:72:487:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:Table 7.3 shows the economic incidence of 98 percent of all taxes levied in the Netherlands 
40:1169:68424:18:18:72:526:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:(distribution of tax shares by decile). These results are based on data from the tax administration and 
40:1170:68528:18:18:72:514:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:on survey data for 1989, 1991 and 1992, respectively. In the early 1990s the top decile paid one-
40:1171:68625:18:18:72:512:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:quarter of all taxes covered, the next 30 percent of households contributed 40 percent of total tax 
40:1172:68725:18:18:72:447:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:revenue, while the bottom half of the distribution generated 24 percent of all taxes.  
40:1173:68811:18:18:72:512:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The personal income tax and net wealth tax are clearly the most progressive levies. On the other 
40:1174:68910:18:18:72:526:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:hand, the local waste management tax - a user fee - is distributed over deciles nearly proportionally.  
40:1175:69013:18:18:72:75:610:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
40:1176:69013:18:18:72:474:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:In the preceding section it has already been pointed out that distributions of taxes paid by 
40:1177:69106:18:18:72:526:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:households in different deciles can present a misleading picture of the progressivity of the tax system, 
40:1178:69211:18:18:72:525:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:because such a presentation takes no account of the different income level in each decile. Therefore, 
40:1179:69312:18:18:72:502:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:Chart 7.2 shows total tax paid by households in each decile as a proportion of aggregate gross 
40:1180:69406:18:18:72:526:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:household income in that decile. On average, households in the Netherlands hand over 60 percent of 
40:1181:69505:18:18:72:524:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:their gross income to the taxman.12 The top two deciles pay only a few percentage points more. The 
40:1182:69604:18:18:72:482:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:bottom two deciles clearly experience somewhat lighter tax burdens, which makes the total 
40:1183:69694:18:18:72:489:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:distribution of tax burdens slightly progressive. Still, even the poorest households on average 
40:1184:69790:18:256:72:321:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:contribute nearly half of their gross income to the fisc.   
40:1185:69849:256:13:72:219:192:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
40:1186:69869:13:14:72:527:179:11:Times:11:Times:F:     12  Taxes  in  the  Netherlands  amount  to  47  percent  of  GDP,  and  absorb  60  percent  of  aggregate  
40:1187:69983:14:13:72:526:165:11:Times:11:Times:F:gross  income  of  private  households.  Various  factors  may  explain  the  difference.  Mainly,  value  added  
40:1188:70097:13:14:72:527:152:11:Times:11:Times:F:tax  (over  6  percent  of  GDP),  retained  corporate  profits  (around  5  percent  of  GDP)  and  investment 
40:1189:70209:14:13:72:526:138:11:Times:11:Times:F:income of pension funds (some 6 percent of GDP) are included in GDP, but none of these components 
40:1190:70307:13:0:72:305:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:is received as current income by private households.

44:1285:74564:18:18:72:508:372:12:Times:12:Times:B:on survey data for 1993.14 The table shows that the top decile pays over 30 percent of the taxes 
44:1286:74661:18:18:72:516:354:12:Times:12:Times:B:covered, the next 40 percent of households generate slightly over 50 percent of total tax revenues, 
44:1287:74761:18:18:72:410:336:12:Times:12:Times:B:while the bottom half of the income distribution contribute only 17 percent. 
44:1288:74837:18:18:72:527:318:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The UK Income Tax, being the most progressive tax, is skewed very strongly to richer households, 
44:1289:74936:18:18:72:494:300:12:Times:12:Times:B:nearly 50 percent is paid by the top decile alone. The tax share paid by the top deciles is also 
44:1290:75033:18:18:72:516:282:12:Times:12:Times:B:relatively high for Social Security taxes (National Insurance) and VAT. National Insurance paid by 
44:1291:75132:18:18:72:512:264:12:Times:12:Times:B:employers is more progressive because there is no ceiling on payments. In comparison, other UK 
44:1292:75227:18:18:72:503:246:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxes and especially excise duties have burdens spread more evenly amongst income deciles. In 
44:1293:75321:18:18:72:496:228:12:Times:12:Times:B:particular, beer and cigarette revenues have burdens that are spread evenly across the income 
44:1294:75415:18:31:72:128:210:12:Times:12:Times:B:distribution.

45:1333:76928:15:18:72:74:348:10:Times:10:Times:F: 
45:1334:76928:18:18:72:524:330:12:Times:12:Times:B:Chart 7.4 shows total taxes paid by households included in each decile as a proportion of aggregate 
45:1335:77028:18:18:72:507:312:12:Times:12:Times:B:gross income in that decile. On average, households pay 43 percent of their gross income to the 
45:1336:77124:18:18:72:502:294:12:Times:12:Times:B:Government in the included taxes. The distribution of payments is strongly progressive. The top 
45:1337:77220:18:18:72:506:276:12:Times:12:Times:B:decile pays several points more (48 percent) while households in lower deciles experience much 
45:1338:77315:18:18:72:507:258:12:Times:12:Times:B:lower average tax burdens. The sharply progressive nature of the UK tax system arises from the 
45:1339:77410:18:18:72:493:240:12:Times:12:Times:B:Income Tax system that exempts significant proportions of many households incomes and yet 
45:1340:77500:18:18:72:525:222:12:Times:12:Times:B:contributes more than a quarter of total government revenue. This very sharp increase in tax burdens 
45:1341:77601:18:18:72:515:204:12:Times:12:Times:B:displayed in Chart 7.4 would be slightly lessened if all taxes were included because the distribution 
45:1342:77703:18:18:72:384:186:12:Times:12:Times:B:of tax shares of the excluded taxes was found to be less progressive. 
45:1343:77772:18:0:72:75:168:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
46:1344:77774:0:15:72:522:440:10:Times:10:Times:F:Note: this chart includes business taxes, customs duties and agricultural levies for which average burdens could 
46:1345:77887:15:15:72:525:425:10:Times:10:Times:F:not be simulated. These taxes account for 15% of tax revenues. Average burdens were therefore calculated using 
46:1346:77998:15:15:72:523:410:10:Times:10:Times:F:the distribution of the tax share, the distribution of gross income and the total tax revenue collected. Because the 
46:1347:78115:15:15:72:499:395:10:Times:10:Times:F:definition of gross income used in the graph gives lower outcomes than administrative figures (for example 
46:1348:78222:15:15:72:518:380:10:Times:10:Times:F:because employer social security contributions are excluded), the impact of these taxes on the overall burden is 
46:1349:78335:15:15:72:119:365:10:Times:10:Times:F:overstated.

49:1419:81369:0:18:72:288:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:8    Incidence of present own EU resources 
49:1420:81411:18:18:72:75:736:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
49:1421:81411:18:18:72:156:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:8.1  Introduction 
49:1422:81428:18:18:72:506:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:Outlays of the European Union are financed from revenue generated by its four `own resources' 
49:1423:81522:18:18:72:516:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:(section 1). Table 8.1 summarizes the revenue structure of the EU. Over the years, the importance 
49:1424:81620:18:18:72:524:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:of agricultural and sugar levies has dwindled to some 3-4 percent of total revenue. In quantitative 
49:1425:81720:18:18:72:522:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:terms, by 1992 customs duties were still the second most important revenue item, bringing in some 
49:1426:81818:18:18:72:511:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:20 percent of total EU revenues. In the early 1990s the 1.4 percent rate on each Member States' 
49:1427:81914:18:18:72:512:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:value-added tax base constituted by far the most important revenue source, generating some 55-
49:1428:82008:18:18:72:463:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:58 percent of total revenue. In years to come, the share of the VAT-resource will fall.  
49:1429:82096:18:18:72:520:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The share of the so-called `fourth own resource' - a GNP-based contribution of Member States 
49:1430:82191:18:18:72:496:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:which in 1991-1992 produced some 13-14 percent of total revenue - will in the future rapidly 
49:1431:82284:18:18:72:513:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:increase. As a consequence of the Edinburgh agreement, the share of this resource is estimated to 
49:1432:82382:18:18:72:225:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:rise to nearly 50 percent in 1999. 
49:1433:82416:18:18:72:521:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Following the approach outlined in section 6.2 and applying the incidence assumptions which have 
49:1434:82515:18:18:72:515:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:also been used to analyze the incidence of national tax systems (section 6.3), this section estimates 
49:1435:82617:18:18:72:511:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:the (economic) incidence of each own resource of the European Union. As before, the analysis is 
49:1436:82713:18:18:72:495:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:restricted to four Member States: Germany, the Netherlands, Spain and the United Kingdom. 
49:1437:82803:18:21:72:420:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:Together, these countries account for over 50 percent of GDP of the Union.  
49:1438:82878:21:15:72:75:409:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
49:1439:82878:15:16:78:373:394:12:Times:12:Times:A:Table 8.1  Tax revenues of the European Community (% share)a) 
49:1440:82939:16:15:78:521:378:12:Times:12:Times:A: 1991 1992 
49:1441:82947:15:15:78:521:363:12:Times:12:Times:A:Agricultural and sugar levies 4 3 
49:1442:82978:15:15:78:521:348:12:Times:12:Times:A:Customs duties 20 19 
49:1443:82996:15:15:78:521:333:12:Times:12:Times:A:Value-added tax base 54 58 
49:1444:83020:15:16:78:521:318:12:Times:12:Times:A:Fourth resource (GNP-base) 13 14 
49:1445:83050:16:19:72:75:302:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
49:1446:83050:19:17:72:491:283:10:Times:10:Times:F:a) Miscellaneous revenues produced 8 percent (1991) and 6 percent (1992) of total revenue; see table 1.1. 
49:1447:83155:17:18:72:75:266:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
49:1448:83155:18:18:72:236:248:12:Times:12:Times:B:8.2  Agricultural and sugar levies 
49:1449:83189:18:18:72:520:230:12:Times:12:Times:B:Regarding the incidence of agricultural and sugar levies no reliable information is available at the EU 
49:1450:83293:18:18:72:506:212:12:Times:12:Times:B:level. It is possible to allocate these taxes in proportion to total consumption, or in line with food 
49:1451:83396:18:18:72:525:194:12:Times:12:Times:B:consumption, using data from national consumer surveys. It follows that to trace the incidence of this 
49:1452:83499:18:18:72:502:176:12:Times:12:Times:B:in itself minor EU revenue source, one additional incidence assumption must be introduced. It is 
49:1453:83596:18:18:72:522:158:12:Times:12:Times:B:assumed here that households pay agricultural and sugar levies in proportion to their consumption of 
49:1454:83697:18:0:72:498:140:12:Times:12:Times:B:food. Arguably, this is a rather strong assumption, but the approach adopted here seems to be 
50:1455:83793:0:18:72:503:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:defensible, especially given the relative limited importance of this traditional own resource of the 
50:1456:83894:18:18:72:152:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:European Union. 
50:1457:83909:18:18:72:517:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Regarding the amount of these levies to be apportioned to Member States, a further complication 
50:1458:84007:18:18:72:516:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:arises because both agricultural levies and customs duties (the two traditional own resources) are 
50:1459:84106:18:18:72:513:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:collected by Member States and transferred to the European Union. Duties are levied at the point 
50:1460:84203:18:18:72:515:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:where taxed goods enter the EU, such as Rotterdam or Antwerp. Since a substantial part of these 
50:1461:84299:18:18:72:513:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:imports are re-exported to other Member States, it would not be correct to allocate all levies and 
50:1462:84398:18:18:72:510:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:customs duties collected by, for example, Dutch tax authorities to households in the Netherlands. 
50:1463:84495:18:18:72:517:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In fact, correcting for the `Rotterdam effect' is not possible, since there is no way "to break down 
50:1464:84597:18:18:72:527:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:duties levied at the Community borders by final inter-Community destination of imports".15 Likewise, 
50:1465:84698:18:18:72:519:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:the group of economic experts holds that "it is virtually impossible to apportion them [i.e. traditional 
50:1466:84803:18:18:72:518:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:resources] by country in a meaningful way".16 For all kind of practical reasons, therefore, we argue 
50:1467:84904:18:18:72:511:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:that aggregate revenues from the two traditional own resources might be apportioned to Member 
50:1468:84998:18:18:72:514:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:States by their share in aggregate EU consumption (on food). Tables 8.2 and 8.3 demonstrate the 
50:1469:85094:18:18:72:397:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:incidence of these resources in four separate Member States, by decile. 
50:1470:85165:18:21:72:75:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:

50:1481:85374:18:18:72:170:302:12:Times:12:Times:B:8.3  Customs duties

51:1503:86214:18:18:72:118:572:12:Times:12:Times:B:8.4  VAT 
51:1504:86222:18:18:72:524:554:12:Times:12:Times:B:The link between the VAT-resource and taxpaying consumers of the European Union is not a direct 
51:1505:86318:18:18:72:523:536:12:Times:12:Times:B:one. The VAT Member States pay into European coffers is not an identifiable part of the VAT paid 
51:1506:86415:18:18:72:512:518:12:Times:12:Times:B:on each purchase. This makes the VAT-resource tantamount to a national contribution calculated 
51:1507:86510:18:18:72:520:500:12:Times:12:Times:B:following an accounting definition of the VAT-base. Although for each Member State the incidence 
51:1508:86607:18:18:72:527:482:12:Times:12:Times:B:of national VAT and the EU VAT-resource will correspond, the VAT-base relative to national GDP 
51:1509:86702:18:18:72:488:464:12:Times:12:Times:B:may show substantial variation. Table 8.4 shows the incidence of the value added tax in four 
51:1510:86795:18:18:72:148:446:12:Times:12:Times:B:Member States.

51:1525:87024:18:18:72:518:207:12:Times:12:Times:B:The incidence of the GNP-based own resource of the European Union is in fact determined by the 
51:1526:87119:18:18:72:524:189:12:Times:12:Times:B:incidence of national tax systems of Member States. Table 8.5 shows the (weighted) incidence of all 
51:1527:87219:18:18:72:524:171:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxes levied in the four Member States. Results presented here refer to the totals on the bottom lines 
51:1528:87322:18:18:72:472:153:12:Times:12:Times:B:of tables 7.2 (Germany), 7.3 (the Netherlands), 7.4 (Spain) and 7.5 (United Kingdom).  
51:1529:87408:18:18:72:506:135:12:Times:12:Times:B:  For a correct interpretation of the information contained in table 8.5 it is very important to note 
51:1530:87510:18:0:72:502:117:12:Times:12:Times:B:that, due to missing data, the incidence of several taxes could not be traced. Indeed, in terms of 
52:1531:87611:0:18:72:471:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:revenue the incidence of only 62 percent of all German taxes has been analyzed. For the 
52:1532:87699:18:18:72:500:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:Netherlands, Spain and the UK the analysis covered 98 percent, 93 percent and 94 percent of 
52:1533:87791:18:18:72:236:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:aggregate tax revenue, respectively. 
52:1534:87827:18:18:72:514:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Given wide differences in national tax mixes, taking into account the spread in taxes covered (62-
52:1535:87927:18:18:72:509:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:98 percent of aggregate tax revenue), and considering the substantial variation in GDP per capita 
52:1536:88025:18:18:72:523:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:(table 4.1) and in the inequality of the distribution of household incomes, the pattern of tax incidence 
52:1537:88130:18:18:72:357:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:in the four countries included in our report is strikingly similar.   
52:1538:88199:18:18:72:524:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The fifty percent poorest households carry 23-24 percent of the aggregate tax burden in Germany, 
52:1539:88298:18:18:72:499:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:the Netherlands and Spain, whereas the ten percent with the highest incomes contribute 25-26 
52:1540:88391:18:18:72:526:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:percent. Only in the United Kingdom, tax burdens are more skewed towards rich households, which 
52:1541:88487:18:18:72:525:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:may perhaps be explained by the greater inequality of the personal income distribution in this country 
52:1542:88590:18:18:72:265:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:and zero-rated items for VAT-purposes.

53:1553:88819:0:18:72:302:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:9. Incidence of prospective own EU resources 
53:1554:88863:18:18:72:75:736:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
53:1555:88863:18:18:72:156:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:9.1  Introduction 
53:1556:88880:18:18:72:523:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:The present four own resources of the European Union will be left unaltered for the period to 1999. 
53:1557:88980:18:18:72:481:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:A number of Member States and the European Parliament have in the past pressed for the 
53:1558:89067:18:18:72:523:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:introduction of a fifth resource, in the form of a Community or Union tax. The European Council has 
53:1559:89167:18:18:72:499:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:explicitly requested the Commission for a report concerning possible candidates for a fifth own 
53:1560:89263:18:18:72:480:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:resource.17 Section 9.2 reviews several proposals for new own resources of the European 
53:1561:89351:18:18:72:490:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:Community. The final section offers estimates of the incidence of one optional own resource. 
53:1562:89443:18:18:72:75:592:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
53:1563:89443:18:18:72:165:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:9.2  Policy options 
53:1564:89462:18:18:72:526:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:In the past the European Parliament has repeatedly called for the introduction of a Community tax as 
53:1565:89563:18:18:72:492:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:a means of ensuring the Community's financial independence. In a recent Working Document 
53:1566:89652:18:18:72:515:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:published under the aegis of the Committee on Budgets of the European Parliament, its rapporteur 
53:1567:89749:18:18:72:521:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:Mr. Horst Langes concludes that of all different tax categories the value-added tax forms the most 
53:1568:89848:18:18:72:506:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:suitable basis so far for a Union tax, as this revenue source is the one most effectively capable of 
53:1569:89949:18:18:72:488:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:meeting the demands of being widespread, simple, transparent and linking taxpayers and the 
53:1570:90040:18:18:72:182:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:destination of the tax.18  
53:1571:90065:18:18:72:521:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:  This Union tax could, for example, take the form of a surcharge of 2 percentage points on national 
53:1572:90166:18:18:72:512:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:VAT-rates of Member States, or alternatively 1.5 points on basic products and 3 points on other 
53:1573:90262:18:18:72:165:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:goods and services. 
53:1574:90281:18:18:72:75:376:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
53:1575:90281:18:18:72:503:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:At the request of the European Commission's Directorates-General for Economic and Financial 
53:1576:90373:18:18:72:510:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:Affairs and for Budgets, a group of independent economists has examined the role of Community 
53:1577:90467:18:18:72:500:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:public finance in the perspective of economic and monetary union. In its report Stable Money--
53:1578:90561:18:18:72:521:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:Sound Finances the expert group discusses a whole range of topics, including the question of what 
53:1579:90659:18:18:72:527:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax categories might be suited to serve as future revenue sources for the European Union. In the end, 
53:1580:90761:18:18:72:303:268:12:Times:12:Times:B:the experts advance three tax options [pp. 88-92]: 
53:1581:90811:18:18:72:512:250:12:Times:12:Times:B:  1. The introduction of a corporate tax on the net cash flow of firms. However, the experts are 
53:1582:90908:18:18:72:524:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:quick to note that as yet the introduction of a cash flow corporate tax is not on the political cards [p. 
53:1583:91014:18:23:72:516:214:12:Times:12:Times:B:89]. Moreover, the datasets used to trace the incidence of existing national tax systems (section 7) 
53:1584:91115:23:14:72:219:191:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
53:1585:91135:14:13:72:526:177:11:Times:11:Times:F:     17  See  Article  10  of  the  Decision  on  new  own  resources  by  the  European  Council,  dated  31  
53:1586:91246:13:26:72:511:164:11:Times:11:Times:F:October 1994 (94/728/EG, Euratom), Journal officiel des Communautés européennes, No L 293/13. 
53:1587:91339:26:13:72:527:138:11:Times:11:Times:F:     18 Committee on Budgets of the European Parliament, Report on a new system of own resources 
53:1588:91436:13:0:72:372:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:for the European Union, DOC EN\RR\250\250479, 8 April, 1994. 
54:1589:91498:0:18:72:521:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:and present EU resources (section 8) do not contain the data that are needed to trace the incidence 
54:1590:91598:18:18:72:515:736:12:Times:12:Times:B:of a new tax, such as a cash flow corporate tax. Therefore, we are not able to trace its distributive 
54:1591:91700:18:18:72:135:718:12:Times:12:Times:B:impacts here. 
54:1592:91713:18:18:72:512:700:12:Times:12:Times:B:  2. The seigniorage of the future European System of Central Banks (ESCB). The greater part of 
54:1593:91809:18:18:72:504:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:the revenue of a central bank stems from its monopoly position as issuer of liabilities carrying no 
54:1594:91909:18:18:72:503:664:12:Times:12:Times:B:remuneration (in the case of bank notes) or one below the market rate of interest (in the case of 
54:1595:92007:18:18:72:521:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:compulsory commercial bank deposits). These liabilities make up the monetary base. Seigniorage is 
54:1596:92105:18:18:72:494:628:12:Times:12:Times:B:the return on interest-bearing assets which form the counterpart to the monetary base [Stable 
54:1597:92199:18:18:72:512:610:12:Times:12:Times:B:Money--Sound Finances, p. 89]. For practical matters, the transfer of central bank profits to the 
54:1598:92297:18:18:72:459:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:government (the only shareholder) is probably the more relevant concept to focus on. 
54:1599:92381:18:18:72:493:574:12:Times:12:Times:B:  We will assume here that new own resources are introduced within a framework of revenue 
54:1600:92471:18:18:72:487:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:neutrality. It follows that to judge the net impact of the introduction of any new resource the 
54:1601:92567:18:18:72:515:538:12:Times:12:Times:B:incidence of this new resource and the incidence of the present resource it (partly) replaces should 
54:1602:92668:18:18:72:507:520:12:Times:12:Times:B:be jointly considered. If the proposal for a seigniorage tax were adopted, Member States would 
54:1603:92763:18:18:72:509:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:miss out on ESCB and national Central Bank profits that would otherwise be remitted to national 
54:1604:92859:18:18:72:526:484:12:Times:12:Times:B:public coffers and be available to finance public outlays. The introduction of this tax would imply that 
54:1605:92964:18:18:72:506:466:12:Times:12:Times:B:the role of the GNP-based own resource would commensurately decrease. Taking the level and 
54:1606:93055:18:18:72:514:448:12:Times:12:Times:B:pattern of public outlays in Member States as given, this policy option implies that Member States 
54:1607:93154:18:18:72:506:430:12:Times:12:Times:B:would have to raise an equivalent amount in higher national taxes. Assuming that the incidence of 
54:1608:93252:18:18:72:523:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:such tax hikes conforms to the present incidence of national tax systems as a whole, the introduction 
54:1609:93354:18:18:72:528:394:12:Times:12:Times:B:of a `seigniorage tax' would in effect not change the present over all incidence of EU own resources.  
54:1610:93456:18:18:72:511:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:  3. The introduction of environmental taxes, and more specifically a tax to reduce the emission of 
54:1611:93556:18:18:72:509:358:12:Times:12:Times:B:carbon dioxide (CO2), or some kind of energy tax. Such taxes should be levied on the basis of a 
54:1612:93652:18:18:72:416:340:12:Times:12:Times:B:harmonized tax base, if they are to qualify as a revenue source to the Union. 
54:1613:93729:18:18:72:75:322:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
54:1614:93729:18:18:72:338:304:12:Times:12:Times:B:9.3  Incidence of a new own resource: value added tax 
54:1615:93782:18:18:72:526:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:This section considers the incidence of one potential new own resource left: a European value added 
54:1616:93882:18:18:72:160:268:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax (see table 9.1). 
54:1617:93902:18:18:72:522:250:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In tracing the incidence of the own VAT resource, we assume that the distribution of the Union tax 
54:1618:94003:18:18:72:496:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:would closely resemble the present distribution of national VAT. This assumption seems to be 
54:1619:94096:18:18:72:482:214:12:Times:12:Times:B:warranted, given that the VAT tax base is effectively harmonised between Member States. 
54:1620:94184:18:18:72:518:196:12:Times:12:Times:B:However, keeping in mind the existing variation of tax rates and in national consumption patterns, it 
54:1621:94286:18:18:72:523:178:12:Times:12:Times:B:must be conceded that incidence patterns presented here are only indicative. On the other hand, we 
54:1622:94385:18:18:72:478:160:12:Times:12:Times:B:have found a strikingly similar distribution of the value-added tax burden for Germany, the 
54:1623:94477:18:18:72:231:142:12:Times:12:Times:B:Netherlands and Spain (table 7.8). 
54:1624:94511:18:0:72:75:124:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
55:1625:94513:0:21:72:75:754:12:Times:12:Times:B:

56:1639:94750:0:15:72:429:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:ANNEX 1  ECONOMIC PROFILES OF FOUR EU MEMBER STATES19 
56:1640:94803:15:15:72:75:742:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
56:1641:94803:15:15:72:144:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:1.A  Germany 
56:1642:94815:15:15:72:467:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:During the 1980s, macro economic trends in the German economy closely mirrored the 
56:1643:94898:15:15:72:500:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:fundamentals of the European business cycle. Table A.1 provides some key information on the 
56:1644:94990:15:15:72:518:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:performance of the German economy after 1980. Initially, the German economy was weakened by 
56:1645:95082:15:15:72:523:667:12:Times:12:Times:B:recessive tendencies in important export-countries, only to recover in the mid 1980s. Great demand 
56:1646:95181:15:15:72:500:652:12:Times:12:Times:B:from abroad as well as growing domestic demand triggered an impressive expansion of private 
56:1647:95273:15:15:72:503:637:12:Times:12:Times:B:investment. As a consequence, the unemployment rate of 7.1 percent [1985] fell to 4.8 percent 
56:1648:95367:15:15:72:490:622:12:Times:12:Times:B:[1990]. In 1990-1991 the reunification of Germany gave a strong boost to the economy and 
56:1649:95456:15:15:72:510:607:12:Times:12:Times:B:compensated for the moment lower demand from abroad. Only in 1992 the worldwide recession 
56:1650:95546:15:15:72:358:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:and internal economic problems resulted in lower growth rates. 
56:1651:95608:15:15:72:517:577:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The rate of inflation over the 1985-1990 period seems to be moderate. In later years the inflation 
56:1652:95709:15:15:72:526:562:12:Times:12:Times:B:rate rose to 4.1 percent because of increasing budget deficits, higher indirect taxes (1991) and wage 
56:1653:95811:15:15:72:523:547:12:Times:12:Times:B:rounds. Higher unemployment in 1992 might be explained by further rationalizations and wage rises, 
56:1654:95910:15:15:72:392:532:12:Times:12:Times:B:as well as be ascribed to structural deficits in the wake of reunification. 
56:1655:95985:15:15:72:508:517:12:Times:12:Times:B:  While in 1980 the fall of the external DM-value forced up import prices - resulting in a negative 
56:1656:96085:15:15:72:491:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:balance of payments - the development after 1985 was exactly the opposite. Since 1991 the 
56:1657:96175:15:15:72:515:487:12:Times:12:Times:B:balance of payments has deteriorated again, as a consequence of increased domestic demand and 
56:1658:96269:15:15:72:222:472:12:Times:12:Times:B:higher imports after reunification. 
56:1659:96304:15:15:72:75:457:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
56:1660:96304:15:16:72:356:442:12:Times:12:Times:B:Table A.1  Economy and public sector, Germany, 1980-1992
