56:1685:96948:13:0:72:279:71:11:Times:11:Times:F:     19 These profiles were written in mid-1994. 
57:1686:96998:0:15:72:508:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:The structure of public outlays has changed, because of higher transfer payments, unemployment 
57:1687:97093:15:15:72:471:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:costs and the enormous investment requirements in the five new federal states (Länder). 
57:1688:97181:15:15:72:521:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:Consequently, the public debt in relation to GDP increased and will probably rise further in the near 
57:1689:97283:15:15:72:104:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:future. 
57:1690:97290:15:15:72:75:697:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
57:1691:97290:15:15:72:75:682:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
57:1692:97290:15:15:72:75:667:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
57:1693:97290:15:15:72:159:652:12:Times:12:Times:B:1.B  Netherlands  
57:1694:97306:15:15:72:514:637:12:Times:12:Times:B:The Dutch economy is both small and extremely open. In 1990 exports and imports of goods and 
57:1695:97399:15:15:72:491:622:12:Times:12:Times:B:services constituted 58 percent and 54 percent of GDP, respectively. After 1980 the current 
57:1696:97491:15:15:72:493:607:12:Times:12:Times:B:balance of payments has continually shown a substantial surplus. Over the past decade, GDP 
57:1697:97582:15:15:72:502:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:growth reflected the worldwide recession of the early 1980s, the ensuing recovery of the world 
57:1698:97677:15:15:72:520:577:12:Times:12:Times:B:economy, and the following economic downturn. On average, over the last ten years annual volume 
57:1699:97773:15:15:72:436:562:12:Times:12:Times:B:growth of GDP hovered around two percent, slightly below the OECD average. 
57:1700:97847:15:15:72:492:547:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Table A.2 provides some additional information on the performance of the Dutch economy. 
57:1701:97937:15:15:72:483:532:12:Times:12:Times:B:Inflation was (far) below the average experience of OECD countries. All told, employment 
57:1702:98026:15:15:72:520:517:12:Times:12:Times:B:measured in constant labour years hardly increased. Nevertheless, after 1983 the economy created 
57:1703:98123:15:15:72:506:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:nearly one million additional jobs. This reflects the marked growth of part-time jobs, and shorter 
57:1704:98222:15:15:72:518:487:12:Times:12:Times:B:working hours. As a result, by 1991 unemployment stood at 7 percent which is not especially high, 
57:1705:98320:15:15:72:519:472:12:Times:12:Times:B:in comparison with the OECD Europe average of 8.6 percent (OECD, [1994], p.A23). However, 
57:1706:98410:15:15:72:518:457:12:Times:12:Times:B:a statistical artefact hides the true size of unemployment, since perhaps as much as a quarter million 
57:1707:98513:15:15:72:506:442:12:Times:12:Times:B:of `hidden' unemployed have been absorbed by public disability programmes. Moreover, higher 
57:1708:98605:15:15:72:527:427:12:Times:12:Times:B:enrolment rates in tertiary education and substantial participation in newly introduced early retirement 
57:1709:98710:15:15:72:267:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:programmes have restricted labour supply. 
57:1710:98751:15:15:72:505:397:12:Times:12:Times:B:  As from the mid 1980s inequality of the personal income distribution has increased, in line with 
57:1711:98850:15:15:72:492:382:12:Times:12:Times:B:trends in several other western industrial countries (UK, USA). Nevertheless, after taxes and 
57:1712:98944:15:15:72:490:367:12:Times:12:Times:B:transfers the personal income distribution in the Netherlands is still flatter than in most OECD 
57:1713:99041:15:15:72:119:352:12:Times:12:Times:B:countries. 
57:1714:99051:15:15:72:75:337:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
57:1715:99051:15:15:72:523:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:The rise of the welfare state has been reflected in a particularly strong growth in public spending and 
57:1716:99155:15:15:72:521:307:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxation levels after the mid 1950s. In the 1960s and early 1970s the expansion of the public sector 
57:1717:99256:15:15:72:483:292:12:Times:12:Times:B:was greatly facilitated by relatively high rates of economic growth. The decline in economic 
57:1718:99349:15:15:72:523:277:12:Times:12:Times:B:performance during the later 1970s and the 1980s triggered a financial crisis of the welfare state. As 
57:1719:99452:15:15:72:507:262:12:Times:12:Times:B:from 1982, the Dutch government has tried to rein in the share of outlays and the deficit in GDP, 
57:1720:99550:15:15:72:517:247:12:Times:12:Times:B:holding the level of taxes and other public sector revenues more or less constant. After ten years of 
57:1721:99652:15:15:72:510:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:restraint, the process of public sector consolidation has clearly met with some success. Improved 
57:1722:99750:15:15:72:504:217:12:Times:12:Times:B:macroeconomic performance and prolonged efforts to effectively curb public spending, enabled 
57:1723:99843:15:15:72:504:202:12:Times:12:Times:B:policymakers to gradually reduce the level of public outlays from 67 percent of GDP in 1983 to 
57:1724:99938:15:15:72:480:187:12:Times:12:Times:B:slightly less than 59 percent of GDP in the early 1990s. Relative to GDP, the public sector 
57:1725:100030:15:15:72:526:172:12:Times:12:Times:B:borrowing requirement fell by more than half, from 9.4 percent of GDP (1982) to some four percent 
57:1726:100128:15:15:72:246:157:12:Times:12:Times:B:of GDP at the beginning of the 1990s.

58:1751:100725:15:15:72:126:429:12:Times:12:Times:B:1.C  Spain 
58:1752:100735:15:15:72:501:414:12:Times:12:Times:B:The growth rate of the Spanish economy has closely followed international trends in the level of 
58:1753:100832:15:15:72:521:399:12:Times:12:Times:B:business activity. Table A.3 summarises the performance of the Spanish economy. After low annual 
58:1754:100929:15:15:72:521:384:12:Times:12:Times:B:growth rates in the first half of the 1980s the economy picked up. In fact, from 1985 till 1991 Spain 
58:1755:101031:15:15:72:513:369:12:Times:12:Times:B:outperformed most other EU economies, its real GDP increasing by about 4 percent per year. As 
58:1756:101125:15:15:72:530:354:12:Times:12:Times:B:from 1992 the economy suffered a period of recession, in line with the general European experience.  
58:1757:101225:15:15:72:482:339:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Despite the economic boom of the second half of the 1980s, in the last decade registered 
58:1758:101316:15:15:72:491:324:12:Times:12:Times:B:unemployment never fell below 16 percent of labour supply. In the 1990s, the number of job 
58:1759:101407:15:15:72:522:309:12:Times:12:Times:B:seekers is sharply up. Over the past decade, initially high inflation levels have gradually come down. 
58:1760:101510:15:15:72:513:294:12:Times:12:Times:B:In the early 1990s, inflation hovered around 6 percent. Policymakers have targeted lower inflation 
58:1761:101609:15:15:72:272:279:12:Times:12:Times:B:rates (3-3.5 percent) for the years to come. 
58:1762:101653:15:15:72:527:264:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The current account of the balance of payments has deteriorated as Spain entered fully into the EU. 
58:1763:101755:15:15:72:505:249:12:Times:12:Times:B:Most observers attribute this trend to an overvalued peseta exchange rate after Spain joined the 
58:1764:101852:15:15:72:503:234:12:Times:12:Times:B:EMS in 1989. Successive devaluations of the peseta have helped to improve the position of the 
58:1765:101946:15:15:72:174:219:12:Times:12:Times:B:balance of payments.

59:1786:102429:12:15:72:457:549:10:Times:10:Times:F:Source: Statistical Annex of European Economy, June 1993; De Haan, Sterks and De Kam [1994] 
59:1787:102520:15:15:72:75:534:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
59:1788:102520:15:15:72:75:519:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
59:1789:102520:15:15:72:75:504:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
59:1790:102520:15:15:72:506:489:12:Times:12:Times:B:A marked expansion of welfare programmes and high priority for public investment and services 
59:1791:102614:15:15:72:517:474:12:Times:12:Times:B:may explain the rapid expansion of the public sector in the Spanish economy. Total outlays shot up 
59:1792:102713:15:15:72:512:459:12:Times:12:Times:B:from 32.5 percent of GDP in 1980 to 46.3 percent in 1992. Tax revenue also strongly increased, 
59:1793:102808:15:15:72:511:444:12:Times:12:Times:B:but not enough to balance the books of the government. The deficit has widened, even during the 
59:1794:102904:15:15:72:514:429:12:Times:12:Times:B:prosperous second half of the 1980s. Due to the recent recession, the gap between public outlays 
59:1795:103001:15:15:72:496:414:12:Times:12:Times:B:and receipts reached nearly 8 percent of GDP in 1994, up from 5 percent of GDP in the early 
59:1796:103093:15:15:72:107:399:12:Times:12:Times:B:1990s. 
59:1797:103099:15:15:72:75:384:12:Times:12:Times:B:

59:1800:103099:15:15:72:179:339:12:Times:12:Times:B:1.D  United Kingdom 
59:1801:103118:15:15:72:512:324:12:Times:12:Times:B:Within Europe, the United Kingdom is a large and industrialised economy. Table A.4 summarises 
59:1802:103212:15:15:72:522:309:12:Times:12:Times:B:the performance of the UK economy. In the 1980s, GDP growth tended to follow world trends but 
59:1803:103306:15:15:72:293:294:12:Times:12:Times:B:in the UK growth rates fluctuated more strongly. 
59:1804:103354:15:15:72:500:279:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The UK economy started and ended the 1980s in the midst of recession. At the trough of the 
59:1805:103447:15:15:72:518:264:12:Times:12:Times:B:recession in 1981, GDP was 5 percent lower than its previous peak in 1979. From 1981 to 1988, 
59:1806:103541:15:15:72:526:249:12:Times:12:Times:B:the economy enjoyed increasing growth rates which peaked at 4.5 percent in 1988. Since then GDP 
59:1807:103637:15:15:72:517:234:12:Times:12:Times:B:growth slowed. The UK was one of the first European countries to experience recession but it has 
59:1808:103734:15:15:72:515:219:12:Times:12:Times:B:also been one of the first to emerge from the recession from the middle of 1992 onward. Over the 
59:1809:103831:15:15:72:523:204:12:Times:12:Times:B:whole cycle (1979-1990), volume GDP growth averaged 2.6 percent per annum. Table A.4 shows 
59:1810:103922:15:15:72:369:189:12:Times:12:Times:B:some additional information on recent trends in the UK economy. 
59:1811:103985:15:15:72:472:174:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Unemployment rates followed changes in GDP but with a significant lag. The number of 
59:1812:104072:15:15:72:517:159:12:Times:12:Times:B:unemployed rose from 4 percent of the labour force at the beginning of 1980 to over 11 percent in 
59:1813:104170:15:15:72:515:144:12:Times:12:Times:B:1986. In the late 1980s, unemployment rates fell rapidly as the economy was growing quickly, but 
59:1814:104267:15:15:72:511:129:12:Times:12:Times:B:the unemployment rate rose above 10 percent again in the early 1990s recession. Throughout the 
59:1815:104362:15:0:72:519:114:12:Times:12:Times:B:period, the composition of the labour force has changed markedly, with increases in service sector, 
60:1816:104464:0:15:72:517:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:female, part-time and self-employed workers and corresponding decreases in the more traditional, 
60:1817:104561:15:15:72:517:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:male full-time industrial jobs. By 1993, women comprised 49 percent of all employees, a rise from 
60:1818:104659:15:15:72:165:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:41 percent in 1979. 
60:1819:104678:15:15:72:524:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:UK retail prices tended to rise faster than the OECD average over the 1980s. They fell from a peak 
60:1820:104777:15:15:72:524:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:above 20 percent in 1980 to an average around 5 percent. After 1990 retail price inflation remained 
60:1821:104877:15:15:72:167:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:below four percent.  
60:1822:104897:15:15:72:498:667:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The current balance of payments deteriorated steadily during the 1980s, as imports rose very 
60:1823:104992:15:15:72:516:652:12:Times:12:Times:B:quickly and the benefit of North-sea oil diminished after 1985. The balance of payments improved 
60:1824:105089:15:15:72:387:637:12:Times:12:Times:B:somewhat in 1990 as the recession reduced the level of UK imports.  
60:1825:105156:15:15:72:506:622:12:Times:12:Times:B:The inequality of personal net incomes has risen sharply since the late 1970s. A consistent series 
60:1826:105255:15:15:72:509:607:12:Times:12:Times:B:shows that the Gini coefficient rose from 0.25 in 1980 to 0.34 in 1991. The rise in inequality was 
60:1827:105354:15:15:72:494:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:caused by many factors. The most important of these were the widening earnings distribution, 
60:1828:105447:15:15:72:497:577:12:Times:12:Times:B:increases in unemployment and self-employment, tax policies pursued and demographic shifts, 
60:1829:105539:15:15:72:263:562:12:Times:12:Times:B:particularly the rise in lone parent families. 
60:1830:105585:15:15:72:75:547:12:Times:12:Times:B:

60:1848:106022:15:15:72:75:276:12:Times:12:Times:B:

60:1850:106053:16:13:72:75:245:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
60:1851:106053:13:12:72:135:232:10:Times:10:Times:F:a) Retail prices. 
60:1852:106070:12:12:72:196:220:10:Times:10:Times:F:b) Goodman and Webb [1994]. 
60:1853:106097:12:12:72:74:208:10:Times:10:Times:F: 
60:1854:106097:12:14:72:459:196:10:Times:10:Times:F:Source: Statistical Annex of European Economy, June 1993; De Haan, Sterks and De Kam [1994]  
60:1855:106189:14:15:72:75:182:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
60:1856:106189:15:15:72:75:167:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
60:1857:106189:15:15:72:75:152:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
60:1858:106189:15:15:72:524:137:12:Times:12:Times:B:The size of the UK public sector has expanded in real terms every year since the second world war, 
60:1859:106288:15:0:72:513:122:12:Times:12:Times:B:except in 1988. However, as a proportion of GDP, public expenditure fell throughout most of the 
61:1860:106386:0:15:72:517:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:1980s reflecting rapid economic growth. Public borrowing in the 1980s also followed trends in the 
61:1861:106484:15:15:72:524:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:economic cycle, with deficits in the early 1980s giving way to surpluses between 1987 and 1990, as 
61:1862:106583:15:15:72:255:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:economic growth swelled tax revenues.  
61:1863:106621:15:15:72:487:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Significant increases in government spending, combined with recessionary effects on public 
61:1864:106714:15:15:72:514:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:expenditure and taxation has transformed a public sector surplus of 3 percent of GDP in 1988-89 
61:1865:106810:15:15:72:512:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:into a deficit approaching 8 percent in 1993-94. Consequently, the debt-to-GDP ratio is climbing 
61:1866:106907:15:0:72:349:667:12:Times:12:Times:B:quickly again, after a period of falling ratios in the late 1980s. 
62:1867:106975:0:15:72:418:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:ANNEX 2  DATA AND MODELS USED TO TRACE TAX BURDENS 
62:1868:107025:15:15:72:75:742:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
62:1869:107025:15:15:72:75:727:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
62:1870:107025:15:15:72:159:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:2.A  Introduction 
62:1871:107042:15:15:72:512:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:This annex details country by country which data and models have been employed to simulate the 
62:1872:107137:15:15:72:502:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:distribution of tax burdens. Section 7.1 already explained the four-step procedure employed to 
62:1873:107232:15:15:72:520:667:12:Times:12:Times:B:allocate taxes to households, which are then ranked into 10 percent groups (`deciles') by increasing 
62:1874:107333:15:15:72:117:652:12:Times:12:Times:B:income.   
62:1875:107342:15:15:72:513:637:12:Times:12:Times:B:  First however, a preliminary note on two key concepts - household and income - seems to be in 
62:1876:107438:15:15:72:487:622:12:Times:12:Times:B:order, since for technical reasons these concepts differ from one country to another, thereby 
62:1877:107532:15:15:72:348:607:12:Times:12:Times:B:complicating cross-country comparisons of tax distributions.  
62:1878:107593:15:15:72:75:592:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
62:1879:107593:15:15:72:186:577:12:Times:12:Times:B:The household concept 
62:1880:107614:15:15:72:510:562:12:Times:12:Times:B:To trace tax incidence in Germany, data have been taken from two surveys. In both the German 
62:1881:107707:15:15:72:519:547:12:Times:12:Times:B:Socio-Economic Panel (GSOEP) and the Income and Consumption Survey (EVS '83) households 
62:1882:107795:15:15:72:351:532:12:Times:12:Times:B:are defined as persons occupying the same dwelling space.20  
62:1883:107854:15:15:72:518:517:12:Times:12:Times:B:  To trace tax incidence in the Netherlands, data have been drawn from three separate surveys. In 
62:1884:107952:15:15:72:515:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:the Panel Survey of Income (PSI) households are tax units, i.e. individuals with full year income. A 
62:1885:108053:15:15:72:515:487:12:Times:12:Times:B:married couple is treated as one tax unit, but individuals who otherwise share a dwelling space are 
62:1886:108153:15:15:72:514:472:12:Times:12:Times:B:each considered as separate tax units and, thus, as separate households. On the other hand, in the 
62:1887:108252:15:15:72:499:457:12:Times:12:Times:B:Consumer Survey and the Housing Demand Survey (HDS) households are defined as persons 
62:1888:108338:15:15:72:509:442:12:Times:12:Times:B:occupying the same dwelling space and sharing their budget(s). Although the household definition 
62:1889:108435:15:15:72:521:427:12:Times:12:Times:B:differs between these three surveys, information from the resulting datasets may be combined, given 
62:1890:108535:15:15:72:323:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:the large overlap of the respective household concepts. 
62:1891:108590:15:15:72:495:397:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In the case of Spain researchers have used data from the Family Expenditure Survey. In this 
62:1892:108684:15:15:72:499:382:12:Times:12:Times:B:survey households are defined as persons occupying the same dwelling space and sharing their 
62:1893:108777:15:15:72:124:367:12:Times:12:Times:B:budget(s).  
62:1894:108788:15:15:72:489:352:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In the Family Expenditure Survey which has been used to trace tax incidence in the United 
62:1895:108880:15:15:72:506:337:12:Times:12:Times:B:Kingdom households are defined as all people living in an accommodation with shared facilities. 
62:1896:108976:15:15:72:524:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:This can comprise more than one family if, for example, elderly relatives live in their children's home, 
62:1897:109081:15:15:72:197:307:12:Times:12:Times:B:or if students live together.  
62:1898:109111:15:15:72:75:292:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
62:1899:109111:15:15:72:171:277:12:Times:12:Times:B:The income concept 
62:1900:109129:15:15:72:496:262:12:Times:12:Times:B:Households are ranked into deciles by increasing income. Economists use various concepts of 
62:1901:109221:15:15:72:114:247:12:Times:12:Times:B:income.  
62:1902:109229:15:15:72:517:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:  First, gross income, which is equal to the algebraic sum of income from labour (including taxable 
62:1903:109329:15:15:72:516:217:12:Times:12:Times:B:perks), from self-employment and from capital (dividends, interest received, and property income, 
62:1904:109427:15:15:72:504:202:12:Times:12:Times:B:including imputed taxable rents from owner-occupied housing), in the form of taxable net capital 
62:1905:109524:15:15:72:523:187:12:Times:12:Times:B:gains (realized capital gains from assets or bequests), and proceeds under private pension plans and 
62:1906:109625:15:20:72:263:172:12:Times:12:Times:B:public sector transfer payments received.  
62:1907:109667:20:14:72:219:152:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
62:1908:109687:14:13:72:526:138:11:Times:11:Times:F:     20  The  Sfb  3/EVS  '83  computations  were  done  together  with  Prof.  Dr.  Hauser  and  Dr.  Faik,  
62:1909:109797:13:0:72:420:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:University of Frankfurt. Their computations are gratefully acknowledged here. 
63:1910:109876:0:15:72:508:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Second, taxable income, which is equal to gross income less deductions for wage earners and 
63:1911:109970:15:15:72:503:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:equivalent deductions for other groups of taxpayers, contributions to private pensions plans and 
63:1912:110067:15:15:72:478:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:(capped) tax deductible mortgage interest and other interest paid. Finally, net income (or: 
63:1913:110159:15:15:72:518:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:disposable income), which is defined as taxable income less social security contributions, personal 
63:1914:110259:15:15:72:468:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:income tax, wealth tax and direct local taxes. Net income may be consumed, or saved.  
63:1915:110344:15:15:72:498:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In the case of Germany, Spain and the United Kingdom households have been ranked into 
63:1916:110431:15:15:72:258:667:12:Times:12:Times:B:deciles on the basis of their net income.  
63:1917:110473:15:15:72:517:652:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In the case of the Netherlands households have been ranked by gross income (PSI) and by net 
63:1918:110567:15:15:72:516:637:12:Times:12:Times:B:income (Consumer Survey, HDS), respectively. Although not ideal, this procedure is nevertheless 
63:1919:110663:15:15:72:488:622:12:Times:12:Times:B:thought to be acceptable, given the close statistical relation between gross and net income of 
63:1920:110758:15:15:72:497:607:12:Times:12:Times:B:households, and because households are lumped together in broad income classes which each 
63:1921:110848:15:15:72:246:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:contain 10 percent of all households.   
63:1922:110887:15:15:72:75:577:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
63:1923:110887:15:15:72:75:562:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
63:1924:110887:15:15:72:75:547:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
63:1925:110887:15:15:72:143:532:12:Times:12:Times:B:2.B  Germany 
63:1926:110899:15:15:72:441:517:12:Times:12:Times:B:Though in Germany many statistics on taxes and transfers are available within the  
63:1927:110981:15:15:72:503:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:Government Department of Finance or within the Statistical Offices, university researchers have 
63:1928:111077:15:15:72:522:487:12:Times:12:Times:B:almost no access to microdata.21 Therefore, the research community has followed its own course to 
63:1929:111175:15:15:72:497:472:12:Times:12:Times:B:obtain the necessary microdata. The former Sonderforschungsbereich 3 (Sfb3) `Microanalytic 
63:1930:111266:15:15:72:490:457:12:Times:12:Times:B:Foundation of Social Policy' at the universities of Frankfurt and Mannheim, for instance, was 
63:1931:111360:15:15:72:492:442:12:Times:12:Times:B:successful in creating new representative surveys for Germany. One outstanding survey is the 
63:1932:111453:15:15:72:490:427:12:Times:12:Times:B:German Socio-Economic Panel (GSOEP) from the Sfb3 and the DIW (German Institute for 
63:1933:111537:15:15:72:504:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:Economic Research, Berlin) which follows in a panel design some 6,000 households (more than 
63:1934:111629:15:15:72:275:397:12:Times:12:Times:B:12,000 persons interviewed), as from 1984. 
63:1935:111671:15:15:72:491:382:12:Times:12:Times:B:  This micro database with personal and household information allows to trace the process of 
63:1936:111764:15:15:72:515:367:12:Times:12:Times:B:income redistribution through tax and public transfer programmes with the help of MICSIM, a PC 
63:1937:111859:15:15:72:526:352:12:Times:12:Times:B:microsimulation model from the former Sfb3, now further developed at the University of Lüneburg.22 
63:1938:111957:15:15:72:510:337:12:Times:12:Times:B:Because of the labour market focus of current research at this University, it is possible to provide 
63:1939:112058:15:15:72:373:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:gross and net income distributional figures based on the GSOEP.   
63:1940:112123:15:15:72:503:307:12:Times:12:Times:B:  If GSOEP data are fed into MICSIM it is possible to simulate the amounts households pay in: 
63:1941:112216:15:15:72:180:292:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  personal income tax; 
63:1942:112239:15:15:72:288:277:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  employee social insurance contributions; and 
63:1943:112286:15:15:72:166:262:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  value-added tax.  
63:1944:112306:15:15:72:430:247:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Thus, the statutory incidence of 62 percent of total tax revenue can be traced. 
63:1945:112387:15:41:72:75:232:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
63:1946:112387:41:14:72:219:191:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
63:1947:112407:14:13:72:526:177:11:Times:11:Times:F:     21  See  the  recent  report  for  the  Ministry  of  Finance  `Microsimulation  for  Tax  Policy  Analysis'  by  
63:1948:112526:13:26:72:291:164:11:Times:11:Times:F:Spahn, Galler, Kaiser, Kassella and Merz [1992]. 
63:1949:112574:26:13:72:526:138:11:Times:11:Times:F:     22  For  a  recent  international  survey  of  microsimulation  principles,  developments  and  applications,  
63:1950:112690:13:0:72:178:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:see Merz [1990; 1991]. 
64:1951:112714:0:15:72:527:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:Data relating to consumption patterns and indirect taxes have been taken from the Einkommens- und 
64:1952:112812:15:15:72:515:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:Verbrauchsstichprobe 1983 (EVS '83). This sample includes 44,507 households, representing 92 
64:1953:112905:15:15:72:258:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:percent of all West-German households. 
64:1954:112943:15:15:72:75:712:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
64:1955:112943:15:15:72:157:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:2.C  Netherlands 
64:1956:112959:15:15:72:508:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:De Kam [1990] discusses datasets and micromodels available in the Netherlands to simulate the 
64:1957:113053:15:15:72:501:667:12:Times:12:Times:B:distribution of tax burdens. No single dataset contains all information needed about income and 
64:1958:113149:15:15:72:446:652:12:Times:12:Times:B:consumption of households. Thus data from several sources have been combined.  
64:1959:113227:15:15:72:481:637:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The most reliable source of information concerning the personal income distribution in the 
64:1960:113320:15:15:72:495:622:12:Times:12:Times:B:Netherlands is the Panel Survey of Income (PSI), which is published annually by the Central 
64:1961:113412:15:15:72:473:607:12:Times:12:Times:B:Bureau of Statistics. For a representative sample of 75,000 households the CBS collects 
64:1962:113500:15:15:72:510:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:demographic and income data from various government administrations. Most income data in the 
64:1963:113593:15:15:72:522:577:12:Times:12:Times:B:sample are from the Tax Administration. The Panel Survey of Income has directly observed data on 
64:1964:113690:15:15:72:190:562:12:Times:12:Times:B:the statutory incidence of: 
64:1965:113717:15:15:72:330:547:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  personal income tax (including wage withholding tax);  
64:1966:113774:15:15:72:175:532:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  net wealth tax; and  
64:1967:113797:15:15:72:222:517:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  general social insurance taxes. 
64:1968:113831:15:15:72:523:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In addition, using data available in the PSI, the CBS has microsimulated employee social insurance 
64:1969:113932:15:15:72:499:487:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxes paid by households and their employers. The most recent PSI available is for year 1991. 
64:1970:114025:15:15:72:490:472:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The CBS also organises an annual Consumer Survey, which offers detailed information on 
64:1971:114114:15:15:72:507:457:12:Times:12:Times:B:patterns of household spending. The number of households in this representative sample is about 
64:1972:114210:15:15:72:498:442:12:Times:12:Times:B:2,000. In the Consumer Survey, some tax payments are directly observed, for example motor 
64:1973:114300:15:15:72:523:427:12:Times:12:Times:B:vehicle tax paid. The amounts households pay in most consumption taxes, notably VAT and various 
64:1974:114396:15:15:72:511:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:excise taxes, can be microsimulated, by applying relevant tax rates to taxable items consumed, as 
64:1975:114494:15:15:72:532:397:12:Times:12:Times:B:reported by households in the sample. The most recent Consumer Survey available is for year 1992.   
64:1976:114593:15:15:72:476:382:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Finally, the Housing Demand Survey (HDS) of the CBS for 1989 contains data on the 
64:1977:114677:15:15:72:517:367:12:Times:12:Times:B:transactions tax, due when property changes hands. The HDS is organised every four years by the 
64:1978:114773:15:15:72:495:352:12:Times:12:Times:B:CBS at the request of the Department of Housing, and has data on some 40,000 households. 
64:1979:114861:15:15:72:520:337:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Combining information from these three datasets, the statutory incidence of 98 percent of all taxes 
64:1980:114963:15:15:72:246:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:(in terms of revenue) has been traced. 
64:1981:115001:15:15:72:75:307:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
64:1982:115001:15:15:72:75:292:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
64:1983:115001:15:15:72:75:277:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
64:1984:115001:15:15:72:126:262:12:Times:12:Times:B:2.D  Spain 
64:1985:115011:15:15:72:525:247:12:Times:12:Times:B:The main dataset used to analyze tax distributions in Spain is the 1990 Family Expenditure Survey 
64:1986:115108:15:15:72:502:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:(Encuesta de Presupuestos Familiares). This representative survey includes a sample of 21,155 
64:1987:115202:15:15:72:503:217:12:Times:12:Times:B:households. The dataset includes information on income, expenditures, living standards (such as 
64:1988:115298:15:15:72:503:202:12:Times:12:Times:B:housing conditions, etcetera) and various socioeconomic characteristics of household members. 
64:1989:115392:15:15:72:515:187:12:Times:12:Times:B:Income is classified by six major monetary and non-monetary sources and by recipient member of 
64:1990:115487:15:15:72:473:172:12:Times:12:Times:B:the household. The dataset offers information about household spending on 226 different 
64:1991:115575:15:15:72:449:157:12:Times:12:Times:B:consumption goods, as well as expenditures on housing (including real investment).  
64:1992:115658:15:15:72:514:142:12:Times:12:Times:B:  From this dataset, under the incidence assumptions made in this report, the statutory incidence of 
64:1993:115759:15:0:72:225:127:12:Times:12:Times:B:the following taxes is calculated:   
65:1994:115797:0:15:72:183:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  personal income tax;  
65:1995:115821:15:15:72:177:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  personal wealth tax; 
65:1996:115844:15:15:72:186:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  corporate income tax; 
65:1997:115868:15:15:72:174:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  other direct taxes;   
65:1998:115892:15:15:72:217:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  social security contributions;  
65:1999:115926:15:15:72:163:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  value-added tax; 
65:2000:115945:15:15:72:144:667:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  excise taxes; 
65:2001:115961:15:15:72:149:652:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  import duties. 
65:2002:115978:15:15:72:75:637:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
65:2003:115978:15:15:72:518:622:12:Times:12:Times:B:Value-added tax and excise taxes has been calculated for each household by applying the effective 
65:2004:116076:15:15:72:507:607:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax rates on their spending on a large desaggregated number of consumption items. The personal 
65:2005:116171:15:15:72:524:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:income tax, as well as social security taxes, have been estimated for each household in the survey by 
65:2006:116273:15:15:72:495:577:12:Times:12:Times:B:applying a micro-fiscal model which captures how legal provisions affect income from various 
65:2007:116366:15:15:72:508:562:12:Times:12:Times:B:sources as reported by households. Other indirect taxes are directly observable from the survey. 
65:2008:116463:15:15:72:483:547:12:Times:12:Times:B:Remaining taxes (import and wealth taxes) included in the analysis has been apportioned to 
65:2009:116554:15:15:72:508:532:12:Times:12:Times:B:households, applying indirect imputation methods and using information as available from various 
65:2010:116651:15:15:72:139:517:12:Times:12:Times:B:other sources. 
65:2011:116665:15:15:72:354:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The above taxes account for 93 percent of total tax revenue. 
65:2012:116727:15:15:72:75:487:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
65:2013:116727:15:15:72:75:472:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
65:2014:116727:15:15:72:75:457:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
65:2015:116727:15:15:72:177:442:12:Times:12:Times:B:2.E  United Kingdom 
65:2016:116746:15:15:72:482:427:12:Times:12:Times:B:The Institute for Fiscal Studies (IFS) calculates the distribution of tax burdens in the United 
65:2017:116842:15:15:72:513:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:Kingdom, using data from the UK Family Expenditure Survey. This survey is collected annually 
65:2018:116935:15:15:72:470:397:12:Times:12:Times:B:by the Central Statistical Office. The resulting dataset contains information about income 
65:2019:117026:15:15:72:347:382:12:Times:12:Times:B:components and spending items of some 7,000 households.  
65:2020:117082:15:15:72:484:367:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Households are ranked according to net income. Gross Income is defined as income from 
65:2021:117170:15:15:72:498:352:12:Times:12:Times:B:employment, self-employment, investments, social security benefits, private pensions, property 
65:2022:117265:15:15:72:520:337:12:Times:12:Times:B:income and other transfers. Income Tax and National insurance are deducted to derive net income. 
65:2023:117362:15:15:72:214:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:Capital gains are not included.  
65:2024:117394:15:15:72:484:307:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Data from FES are fed into a micromodel (TAXBEN2) to simulate tax payments for each 
65:2025:117480:15:15:72:488:292:12:Times:12:Times:B:household. Johnson, Stark and Webb [1990] describe the IFS Tax and Benefit Model. The 
65:2026:117566:15:15:72:210:277:12:Times:12:Times:B:following taxes are calculated: 
65:2027:117597:15:15:72:180:262:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  personal income tax; 
65:2028:117620:15:15:72:231:247:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  national insurance contributions; 
65:2029:117656:15:15:72:163:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  value-added tax; 
65:2030:117675:15:15:72:231:217:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  various other indirect taxes; and 
65:2031:117711:15:15:72:155:202:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  the council tax. 
65:2032:117730:15:15:72:426:187:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In total IFS can thus directly model 94 percent of total government revenue.  
65:2033:117809:15:15:72:75:172:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
65:2034:117809:15:15:72:487:157:12:Times:12:Times:B:The IFS Tax and Benefit model simulates tax payments and benefit receipts. It does not use 
65:2035:117900:15:15:72:526:142:12:Times:12:Times:B:recorded payments and receipts from the Family Expenditure Survey, because its usual function is to 
65:2036:118000:15:0:72:525:127:12:Times:12:Times:B:analyze the distributional effect of reforms to the tax and benefit system and because some taxes and 
66:2037:118104:0:15:72:520:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:benefits are recorded inaccurately in the FES. The simulation is complex. Calculations are made for 
66:2038:118204:15:15:72:483:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:each tax and benefit and for interactions between UK taxes and benefits. Indirect taxes are 
66:2039:118296:15:15:72:525:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:calculated from household expenditures on VAT and excised goods. House prices are imputed from 
66:2040:118391:15:15:72:520:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:a regression on household characteristics and council tax values are calculated on the basis of these 
66:2041:118493:15:15:72:225:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:prices and the households region. 
66:2042:118526:15:15:72:75:682:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
66:2043:118526:15:0:72:75:667:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
67:2044:118528:0:15:72:375:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:ANNEX 3  SENSITIVITY ANALYSIS OF TAX INCIDENCE 
67:2045:118574:15:15:72:75:742:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
67:2046:118574:15:15:72:75:727:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
67:2047:118574:15:15:72:524:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:This annex discusses the sensitivity of results that have been presented in the main text for alternative 
67:2048:118680:15:15:72:510:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:specifications of the shifting assumptions. We consider the corporate income tax, employer social 
67:2049:118778:15:15:72:509:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:insurance contributions and the local property tax, respectively. In one specification it is assumed 
67:2050:118879:15:15:72:486:667:12:Times:12:Times:B:that these taxes especially hit consumers. Another specification assumes that these taxes are 
67:2051:118973:15:15:72:269:652:12:Times:12:Times:B:predominantly borne by owners of capital.  
67:2052:119015:15:15:72:75:637:12:Times:12:Times:B:

67:2073:119378:15:15:72:521:320:12:Times:12:Times:B:established assuming that shareholders, recipients of property income and consumers each shoulder

67:2076:119633:15:15:72:490:275:12:Times:12:Times:B:  From the tables below it follows that the over-all distribution of tax shares hardly changes if

69:2109:120528:0:15:72:410:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:ANNEX 4  TAX SHIFTING IN MACROECONOMETRIC MODELS 
69:2110:120576:15:15:72:75:742:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
69:2111:120576:15:15:72:75:727:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
69:2112:120576:15:15:72:144:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:4.A  Germany 
69:2113:120588:15:15:72:521:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:The Deutsche Bundesbank runs a macroeconometric model. This model is a quarterly dynamic and 
69:2114:120681:15:15:72:508:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:interdependent system of the German economy. The current version has a total of 331 equations 
69:2115:120775:15:15:72:487:667:12:Times:12:Times:B:(120 of which are behavioural equations). The model contains a simulation block for eastern 
69:2116:120867:15:15:72:506:652:12:Times:12:Times:B:Germany. While part of the model is based on neo-Keynesian theory, increased attention is also 
69:2117:120962:15:15:72:491:637:12:Times:12:Times:B:paid to long-term equilibrium aspects. So far, the model follows `mainstream economics' and 
69:2118:121054:15:15:72:264:622:12:Times:12:Times:B:contains elements of both theoretical lines. 
69:2119:121098:15:15:72:322:607:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Taxes are not directly included in the wage equations. 
69:2120:121154:15:15:72:506:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Prices depend on specific indirect tax rates. Negotiated monthly wages in turn are a function of 
69:2121:121253:15:15:72:525:577:12:Times:12:Times:B:consumption prices, and, hence, indirectly of indirect taxes. Direct taxes are included in the definition 
69:2122:121359:15:15:72:523:562:12:Times:12:Times:B:of disposable income, labour force participation and investment. Again, the effect of taxes on wages 
69:2123:121460:15:15:72:143:547:12:Times:12:Times:B:is only indirect. 
69:2124:121477:15:15:72:522:532:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Direct tax receipts are disaggregated in the model into wage tax, assessed income tax, corporation 
69:2125:121578:15:15:72:507:517:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax and other direct taxes (property tax, investment income tax, motor vehicle tax, etc.). Indirect 
69:2126:121678:15:15:72:512:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxes are divided into value-added tax, mineral oil tax, trade tax and other indirect taxes (customs 
69:2127:121779:15:15:72:496:487:12:Times:12:Times:B:duties, tobacco tax, spirits tax, taxes on land and buildings, capital transaction taxes: securities 
69:2128:121880:15:15:72:509:472:12:Times:12:Times:B:transfer tax, company tax, insurance and stamp taxes, etc.). Social security contributions are split 
69:2129:121981:15:15:72:280:457:12:Times:12:Times:B:into employees' and employers' contributions. 
69:2130:122026:15:15:72:512:442:12:Times:12:Times:B:In addition to income effects, tax measures also have cost effects. The extent to which enterprises 
69:2131:122126:15:15:72:519:427:12:Times:12:Times:B:use their capacity to produce goods depends inter alia on the cost involved in employing the capital 
69:2132:122227:15:15:72:103:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:stock. 
69:2133:122233:15:15:72:503:397:12:Times:12:Times:B:  While an increase in enterprises' direct taxes directly raises the tax burden of firms, it indirectly 
69:2134:122337:15:15:72:494:382:12:Times:12:Times:B:increases the relief given in the form of tax deductible costs. Under the conditions prevailing in 
69:2135:122436:15:15:72:524:367:12:Times:12:Times:B:Germany as regards tax rates, interest rates and depreciation rules, the net effect is that user costs of 
69:2136:122542:15:15:72:486:352:12:Times:12:Times:B:capital tend to decrease slightly if direct taxes are increased. Other influences will, however, 
69:2137:122639:15:15:72:384:337:12:Times:12:Times:B:ultimately lead to lower capital spending if direct taxes are increased. 
69:2138:122711:15:15:72:524:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The production costs of enterprises are made up of wage costs, the costs of using the capital stock 
69:2139:122813:15:15:72:524:307:12:Times:12:Times:B:and import prices. The burden of indirect taxes which initially likewise have to be borne by firms has 
69:2140:122916:15:15:72:524:292:12:Times:12:Times:B:to be added. The extent to which enterprises will be able to pass on their costs to buyers depends in 
69:2141:123018:15:15:72:379:277:12:Times:12:Times:B:particular on the market situation and the price elasticity of demand. 
69:2142:123088:15:15:72:497:262:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Most increases in production costs resulting from a rise of wage costs, capital user costs and 
69:2143:123185:15:15:72:501:247:12:Times:12:Times:B:import prices or in the indirect tax burden are passed on by enterprises through their prices in a 
69:2144:123284:15:15:72:523:232:12:Times:12:Times:B:lengthy adjustment process.23 Prices then in turn affect wages, profits, interest rates and transactions 
69:2145:123389:15:15:72:520:217:12:Times:12:Times:B:and thus feed back onto the various tax assessment bases and other macroeconomic variables such 
69:2146:123485:15:23:72:467:202:12:Times:12:Times:B:as output and employment. The extent to which changes in tax rates or in social security 
69:2147:123574:23:14:72:219:179:12:Courier:11:Times:C:                     
69:2148:123594:14:13:72:526:165:11:Times:11:Times:F:     23  Since  the  demand  for  goods  does  not  react  with  complete  inelasticity  to  price  changes  a  full  
69:2149:123712:13:14:72:527:152:11:Times:11:Times:F:pass-on  of  costs  is  not  possible.  The  higher  the  price  elasticity  of  demand,  the  smaller  the  scope  for  
69:2150:123833:14:13:72:526:138:11:Times:11:Times:F:passing  on  costs  and  indirect  tax  increases.  The  price  functions  of  the  model  have  been  described  in  
69:2151:123951:13:0:72:275:125:11:Times:11:Times:F:more detail in Schlesinger and Jahnke [1987]. 
70:2152:123998:0:15:72:496:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:contributions will ultimately affect the economic situation will therefore depend on the dynamic 
70:2153:124095:15:15:72:219:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:interdependencies of the model. 
70:2154:124126:15:15:72:75:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:

70:2179:124987:17:15:72:75:393:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
70:2180:124987:15:15:72:75:378:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
70:2181:124987:15:15:72:511:363:12:Times:12:Times:B:Two different simulations are carried out to analyze the probable aggregate effects of these taxes, 
70:2182:125087:15:15:72:503:348:12:Times:12:Times:B:with wage, assessed income and corporation tax representing the impact of direct taxes and the 
70:2183:125182:15:15:72:502:333:12:Times:12:Times:B:value-added tax the effects of indirect taxes (see Jahnke, [1994]). The tax increase first of all is 
70:2184:125283:15:15:72:333:318:12:Times:12:Times:B:reflected in a decrease of households' disposable income. 
70:2185:125340:15:15:72:520:303:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Lower demand for goods decreases output and employment. Capacity utilisation deteriorates and 
70:2186:125436:15:15:72:396:288:12:Times:12:Times:B:unemployment increases. This triggers some wage and price decreases. 
70:2187:125504:15:15:72:512:273:12:Times:12:Times:B:But as time proceeds, the real effects vanish and real GNP returns to the baseline scenario. In the 
70:2188:125604:15:15:72:348:258:12:Times:12:Times:B:long run there are no aggregate effects of raising direct taxes. 
70:2189:125668:15:15:72:477:243:12:Times:12:Times:B:Ultimately, an increase in direct tax rates has no adverse influence on the real growth rate. 
70:2190:125761:15:15:72:504:228:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Just as in the case of higher direct taxes, the original impulse would increase considerably over 
70:2191:125861:15:15:72:510:213:12:Times:12:Times:B:time. The simulations with the model indicate that initially firms will be able to pass on only part of 
70:2192:125965:15:15:72:513:198:12:Times:12:Times:B:the extra cost through higher selling prices. Consequently, a considerable part of any value-added 
70:2193:126064:15:15:72:336:183:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax increase temporarily reduces the profits of enterprises. 
70:2194:126124:15:15:72:75:168:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
70:2195:126124:15:15:72:517:153:12:Times:12:Times:B:Although any value-added tax increase directly adds to the indirect tax burden of firms, even in the 
70:2196:126225:15:0:72:516:138:12:Times:12:Times:B:longer run only part of these extra costs can be passed on because there is a simultaneous adverse 
71:2197:126326:0:15:72:526:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:impact on real demand. The simulations show that only 40 percent of a value-added tax increase will 
71:2198:126426:15:15:72:245:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:be passed on in prices in the long run. 
71:2199:126465:15:15:72:508:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:  After a few years, there will be a self-adjustment here too. The rate of real growth returns to its 
71:2200:126567:15:15:72:524:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:rate in the baseline scenario. The decline in real growth, in the meantime, exerts smoothing effects on 
71:2201:126671:15:15:72:523:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:the price increase. In the long run, i.e. after seven years, real GDP has returned to its baseline value, 
71:2202:126777:15:15:72:314:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:whereas the price level has increased by 0.4 percent. 
71:2203:126830:15:15:72:522:667:12:Times:12:Times:B:  An increase in the value-added tax rate, ultimately has no adverse effects on real output, but raises 
71:2204:126934:15:15:72:141:652:12:Times:12:Times:B:the price level. 
71:2205:126950:15:15:72:75:637:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
71:2206:126950:15:15:72:75:622:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
71:2207:126950:15:15:72:75:607:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
71:2208:126950:15:15:72:177:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:4.B  The Netherlands 
71:2209:126970:15:15:72:517:577:12:Times:12:Times:B:The effect of taxes on the wage level is very important in the most recent macroeconometric model 
71:2210:127068:15:15:72:523:562:12:Times:12:Times:B:of the Central Planning Bureau (CPB). In this model, best known under its acronym FKSEC [CPB, 
71:2211:127162:15:15:72:494:547:12:Times:12:Times:B:1992], wages are modelled at the macro level and depend on labour productivity, a weighted 
71:2212:127253:15:15:72:525:532:12:Times:12:Times:B:average of consumer and producer prices, taxes and social insurance contributions, the level and the 
71:2213:127354:15:15:72:500:517:12:Times:12:Times:B:change of the unemployment rate, and the replacement ratio. In fact, taxes and social insurance 
71:2214:127450:15:15:72:517:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:contributions have always been part of wage equations in Dutch econometric models. Public levies 
71:2215:127547:15:15:72:479:487:12:Times:12:Times:B:are divided between the share paid by employers and by employees, since "this distinction 
71:2216:127637:15:15:72:500:472:12:Times:12:Times:B:consistently appears to be relevant empirically, and probably indicates some degree of nominal 
71:2217:127732:15:15:72:343:457:12:Times:12:Times:B:rigidity in the wage formation process" [CPB, 1992, p.31].  
71:2218:127791:15:15:72:509:442:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The main theoretical underpinning of the wage equation is a general type of bargaining model, in 
71:2219:127890:15:15:72:527:427:12:Times:12:Times:B:which the wage rate is determined as the outcome of a bargaining process between firms and unions. 
71:2220:127989:15:15:72:442:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:The relevant parts of the equation for the growth of the wage rate read as follows: 
71:2221:128072:15:15:72:75:397:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
71:2222:128072:15:19:72:521:382:12:Times:12:Times:B:wage = 0,50pc +0,50pyfr ... + 0,36[Dsll/(1 - sll1) + Dttl/(1 - tll1)]  - 0,20 [Dslw/(1 + slw1)] 
71:2223:128161:19:15:72:75:363:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
71:2224:128161:15:15:72:505:348:12:Times:12:Times:B:where pc and pyfr represent the growth rate of the prices of private consumption and gross value-
71:2225:128258:15:15:72:493:333:12:Times:12:Times:B:added of the enterprise sector, respectively; sll denotes social insurance contributions paid by 
71:2226:128355:15:15:72:482:318:12:Times:12:Times:B:employees as a fraction of gross wages; ttl represents direct taxes on wage income paid by 
71:2227:128446:15:15:72:517:303:12:Times:12:Times:B:employees as a fraction of the total wage bill minus social insurance contributions, and slw denotes 
71:2228:128547:15:15:72:387:288:12:Times:12:Times:B:employers social insurance contributions as a fraction of gross wages. 
71:2229:128617:15:15:72:508:273:12:Times:12:Times:B:  It is interesting, that in the present model of the CPB the coefficients for the wage tax and social 
71:2230:128720:15:15:72:517:258:12:Times:12:Times:B:insurance contributions are larger than in previous models, which implies that the incidence of these 
71:2231:128822:15:15:72:527:243:12:Times:12:Times:B:levies is more evenly divided between employers and employees. According to information provided 
71:2232:128919:15:15:72:521:228:12:Times:12:Times:B:by the CPB, the present coefficient has been calibrated on the basis of estimates for various sample 
71:2233:129020:15:15:72:513:213:12:Times:12:Times:B:periods with different wage regimes, and on the basis of the historical tracking performance of the 
71:2234:129120:15:15:72:524:198:12:Times:12:Times:B:model. This outcome is not so amazing as it perhaps may appear at first glance. It is well known that 
71:2235:129222:15:15:72:513:183:12:Times:12:Times:B:the degree of tax shifting in the wage equation is not very stable over time and depends very much 
71:2236:129321:15:15:72:524:168:12:Times:12:Times:B:on the estimation period. Indeed, Brunia and Kuper [1990] conclude that shifting of taxes and social 
71:2237:129422:15:15:72:510:153:12:Times:12:Times:B:insurance contributions has gradually diminished, whereas on the other hand shifting of employers 
71:2238:129520:15:0:72:245:138:12:Times:12:Times:B:contributions has increased over time. 
72:2239:129560:0:15:72:525:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:Table A.8 shows the simulation outcomes of a reduction in income taxes by 1 percent of net national 
72:2240:129660:15:15:72:518:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:income, which is financed by issuing government debt. The entries in the table show the differences 
72:2241:129760:15:15:72:258:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:between the simulation and the base run. 
72:2242:129800:15:15:72:75:712:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
72:2243:129800:15:15:72:75:697:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
72:2244:129800:15:16:72:480:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:Table A.8  Cumulated effects of a reduction in income taxes by 1% of net national income 
72:2245:129888:16:15:72:75:666:12:Times:12:Times:B:

72:2247:129900:15:15:72:75:636:12:Times:12:Times:B:

72:2254:130074:14:15:72:75:533:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
72:2255:130074:15:15:72:75:518:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
72:2256:130074:15:15:72:75:503:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
72:2257:130074:15:15:72:525:488:12:Times:12:Times:B:It follows from table A.8 that - after wage negotiations - according to the FKSEC-model the tax cut 
72:2258:130174:15:15:72:523:473:12:Times:12:Times:B:will be partly passed on to employers in the form of lower contractual wages. Lower labour costs in 
72:2259:130274:15:15:72:502:458:12:Times:12:Times:B:turn lead to lower prices. Moreover, table A.8 indicates that the distribution of income between 
72:2260:130371:15:15:72:523:443:12:Times:12:Times:B:capital and labour also changes. Initially, the share of labour decreases by 0.5 percentage point, and 
72:2261:130474:15:15:72:231:428:12:Times:12:Times:B:eventually to 0.2 percentage point. 
72:2262:130509:15:15:72:75:413:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
72:2263:130509:15:15:72:525:398:12:Times:12:Times:B:The MIMIC-model (MIcro-Macro model to analyze the Institutional Context), which the CPB uses 
72:2264:130602:15:15:72:511:383:12:Times:12:Times:B:for medium-term simulations only, is an applied general equilibrium model [Gelauff, 1992; Gelauff 
72:2265:130700:15:15:72:510:368:12:Times:12:Times:B:and Graafland, 1994]. Like in FKSEC, the bargaining approach is taken to model the process of 
72:2266:130794:15:15:72:518:353:12:Times:12:Times:B:wage formation. The wage outcome of the model depends on consumer prices, the average rate of 
72:2267:130888:15:15:72:507:338:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxes and social insurance contributions, the net replacement ratio, the marginal rate of taxes and 
72:2268:130988:15:15:72:526:323:12:Times:12:Times:B:premiums, the unemployment rate and search costs of employers. A higher average tax rate triggers 
72:2269:131086:15:15:72:521:308:12:Times:12:Times:B:wage demands to compensate for the loss of utility derived from a workers job. A higher marginal 
72:2270:131182:15:15:72:396:293:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax rate reduces the marginal utility of wages and lowers the wage rate.  
72:2271:131255:15:15:72:518:278:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The parameters of the model are set in such a way that the elasticities of the explanatory variables 
72:2272:131358:15:15:72:522:263:12:Times:12:Times:B:are in accordance with empirical estimates of the wage equation for the Netherlands. In the model a 
72:2273:131458:15:15:72:510:248:12:Times:12:Times:B:1 percent increase in average and marginal tax rates leads to a change of 0.60 percent and -0.09 
72:2274:131555:15:15:72:513:233:12:Times:12:Times:B:percent of the wage rate, respectively. A 1 percent increase in consumer prices makes wages rise 
72:2275:131652:15:15:72:150:218:12:Times:12:Times:B:by 0.49 percent. 
72:2276:131668:15:15:72:519:203:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Table A.9 shows simulation outcomes of the MIMIC-model if taxes are reduced by Gld 1bn, this 
72:2277:131763:15:15:72:517:188:12:Times:12:Times:B:tax cut being financed by a corresponding decline in government non-wage consumption spending. 
72:2278:131858:15:15:72:357:173:12:Times:12:Times:B:The government may alternatively use the available Gld 1bn to: 
72:2279:131920:15:15:72:527:158:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  reduce the tax rate of the first bracket by 0.6 percentage points; (1) 
72:2280:131992:15:15:72:527:143:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  lower the tax rate of the second bracket by 3.1 percentage points; (2) 
72:2281:132064:15:15:72:527:128:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  reduce the tax rate of the third bracket by 7.4 percentage points; (3) 
72:2282:132136:15:0:72:527:113:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  increase the ceiling of the second bracket by Gld 1,600; (4) 
73:2283:132200:0:15:72:527:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  raise the ceiling of the third bracket by Gld 45,800; (5) 
73:2284:132259:15:15:72:527:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  increase the basic personal allowance by Gld 270; (6) 
73:2285:132314:15:15:72:543:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:o  reduce the basic VAT-rate by 0.8 percentage points (7)

73:2295:132730:16:13:72:75:575:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
73:2296:132730:13:12:72:160:562:10:Times:10:Times:F:a) Percentage change 
73:2297:132750:12:12:72:74:550:10:Times:10:Times:F: 
73:2298:132750:12:14:72:219:538:10:Times:10:Times:F:Source: Gelauff and Graafland [1994] 
73:2299:132786:14:15:72:75:524:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
73:2300:132786:15:15:72:75:509:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
73:2301:132786:15:15:72:489:494:12:Times:12:Times:B:Reducing the tax rate of the first bracket increases labour supply, and lowers the wage level. 
73:2302:132881:15:15:72:506:479:12:Times:12:Times:B:Furthermore, the average tax rate drops, which reduces wage demands. In the second and third 
73:2303:132974:15:15:72:509:464:12:Times:12:Times:B:variant wages fall less, due to the smaller increase of labour supply. Other reasons for the smaller 
73:2304:133075:15:15:72:526:449:12:Times:12:Times:B:decline of the wage rate in these variants, in comparison with the first variant, are the larger reduction 
73:2305:133182:15:15:72:508:434:12:Times:12:Times:B:of the marginal tax rate and the smaller decline of the average tax. Variants four and five evoke a 
73:2306:133282:15:15:72:524:419:12:Times:12:Times:B:higher supply of labour, albeit in varying degrees. In the sixth variant the wage rate goes up, because 
73:2307:133386:15:15:72:486:404:12:Times:12:Times:B:of the negative income effect experienced by both the breadwinner and his/her partner. This 
73:2308:133478:15:15:72:511:389:12:Times:12:Times:B:alternative also leads to higher social insurance contributions, which also puts upward pressure an 
73:2309:133578:15:15:72:494:374:12:Times:12:Times:B:wages. Finally, it is interesting to note that in the MIMIC-model a lower value-added tax rate 
73:2310:133673:15:15:72:357:359:12:Times:12:Times:B:reduces consumer prices and thereby restrains wage demands. 
73:2311:133732:15:15:72:75:344:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
73:2312:133732:15:15:72:75:329:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
73:2313:133732:15:15:72:75:314:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
73:2314:133732:15:15:72:126:299:12:Times:12:Times:B:4.C  Spain 
73:2315:133742:15:15:72:499:284:12:Times:12:Times:B:The so called MOISEES model (see Molinas et al., [1990] and Andres, Dolado, Molinas and 
73:2316:133830:15:15:72:493:269:12:Times:12:Times:B:Zabalza, [1990]) is an integrated general equilibrium macroeconometric model of the Spanish 
73:2317:133922:15:15:72:495:254:12:Times:12:Times:B:economy. The model was built by the General Planning Division as a tool to simulate and help 
73:2318:134015:15:15:72:472:239:12:Times:12:Times:B:evaluate the consequences of most of the more important macroeconomic policies of the 
73:2319:134101:15:15:72:335:224:12:Times:12:Times:B:administration, including budgetary and monetary policies. 
73:2320:134159:15:15:72:486:209:12:Times:12:Times:B:  In this model, nominal wages are understood as the result of a bargaining process between 
73:2321:134251:15:15:72:526:194:12:Times:12:Times:B:employers and employees (see Dolado, Malo de Molina and Zabalza [1986]). Since the outcome of 
73:2322:134345:15:15:72:523:179:12:Times:12:Times:B:this process depends upon the relative power of both parties, the wage equation, one of the building 
73:2323:134446:15:15:72:499:164:12:Times:12:Times:B:blocks of the simultaneous equations of the model, includes a vector Z of exogenous variables, 
73:2324:134541:15:15:72:521:149:12:Times:12:Times:B:which along with indirect taxes and other variables that may affect nominal wages, includes a subset 
73:2325:134642:15:15:72:526:134:12:Times:12:Times:B:of variables concerning the decision to participate or not in the labour market, and the strength of the 
73:2326:134747:15:0:72:293:119:12:Times:12:Times:B:unions. The form of the equation is the following: 
74:2327:134799:0:15:72:75:757:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
74:2328:134799:15:15:72:441:742:12:Times:12:Times:B: log W = ao + al log P + a2 log(K(-1)/ L) + a3 log(1 + TEMCS) - a4v + a5Z 
74:2329:134871:15:15:72:75:727:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
74:2330:134871:15:15:72:488:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:where W is nominal wage cost, P is a GNP deflator price, K(-1)/L is a proxy for the labour 
74:2331:134962:15:15:72:515:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:productivity level, V is the unemployment rate, TEMCS is the effective social security rate paid by 
74:2332:135062:15:15:72:424:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:the employers, and Z is the vector with exogenous variables discussed above. 
74:2333:135138:15:15:72:511:667:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The wage equation of the MOISEES model together with a GNP deflator equation is estimated 
74:2334:135230:15:15:72:516:652:12:Times:12:Times:B:(by three stage least squares) using log(W/P (1+TEMCS)) as the dependent variable, so the value 
74:2335:135326:15:15:72:522:637:12:Times:12:Times:B:of the coefficient a3 is lost. Using the dataset of the model (years 1964-1988) we have estimated by 
74:2336:135427:15:15:72:515:622:12:Times:12:Times:B:OLS a3, getting a value of 0.3. This parameter has also been estimated by Escobedo [1991], who 
74:2337:135522:15:15:72:513:607:12:Times:12:Times:B:applied a simultaneous model for the Spanish economy and obtained a value of 0.35, which is not 
74:2338:135618:15:15:72:159:592:12:Times:12:Times:B:very far from ours. 
74:2339:135637:15:15:72:75:577:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
74:2340:135637:15:15:72:517:562:12:Times:12:Times:B:Although we are tempted to conclude that the incidence hypothesis used in the text does not match 
74:2341:135735:15:15:72:488:547:12:Times:12:Times:B:the value of a3, at least two observations are in order. First, our shifting hypothesis has to be 
74:2342:135833:15:15:72:514:532:12:Times:12:Times:B:considered as the result of a long run equilibrium situation of the economy; and second, we should 
74:2343:135932:15:15:72:514:517:12:Times:12:Times:B:take into account that the legal changes, introduced in the Spanish economy during the late 1980's 
74:2344:136031:15:15:72:504:502:12:Times:12:Times:B:and 1990's, have injected a greater flexibility into the labour market, with firms having more and 
74:2345:136130:15:15:72:500:487:12:Times:12:Times:B:more bargaining power over the unions. This is shown by several studies on the Spanish labour 
74:2346:136224:15:15:72:527:472:12:Times:12:Times:B:market (see for instance: Bentolila and Dolado [1992]) and by tests of an insider-outsider model like 
74:2347:136326:15:15:72:223:457:12:Times:12:Times:B:Nickell and Wadhwani's (1990). 
74:2348:136356:15:15:72:522:442:12:Times:12:Times:B:  We finally consider a simulation run with the MOISEES model, which consists of a permanent rise 
74:2349:136454:15:15:72:520:427:12:Times:12:Times:B:by 10 percent of the social security tax rates paid by employers, while additional revenues are used 
74:2350:136555:15:15:72:518:412:12:Times:12:Times:B:to redeem some of the outstanding public debt. This allows an assessment of the full impact of such 
74:2351:136655:15:15:72:504:397:12:Times:12:Times:B:a policy from a general equilibrium point of view (i.e. direct and indirect effects of the measure). 
74:2352:136755:15:15:72:521:382:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Table A.10 illustrates the impacts of this policy change on various macroeconomic variables of the 
74:2353:136856:15:15:72:519:367:12:Times:12:Times:B:Spanish economy. The numbers indicate changes with respect to the values predicted by the model 
74:2354:136952:15:15:72:395:352:12:Times:12:Times:B:under no policy changes, which is considered the reference equilibrium. 
74:2355:137023:15:15:72:75:337:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
74:2356:137023:15:15:72:75:322:12:Times:12:Times:B:

75:2372:137595:12:14:72:149:732:10:Times:10:Times:F:percentage points.

75:2375:137654:14:15:72:75:691:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
75:2376:137654:15:15:72:75:676:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
75:2377:137654:15:15:72:75:661:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
75:2378:137654:15:15:72:505:646:12:Times:12:Times:B:The equilibrium nature of these results should be emphasized. In the short run, the policy change 
75:2379:137752:15:15:72:509:631:12:Times:12:Times:B:raises prices by 2.2 percentage points, with almost no change in the long run. This means that the 
75:2380:137851:15:15:72:518:616:12:Times:12:Times:B:average effect on prices is certainly small, because this policy measure tends to push up real labour 
75:2381:137953:15:15:72:518:601:12:Times:12:Times:B:costs, both in the short and in the long run, which in turn reduces employment by -2.4 percent, and 
75:2382:138053:15:15:72:399:586:12:Times:12:Times:B:lowers aggregate demand and real GDP by -1.6 percent in the long run. 
75:2383:138121:15:15:72:515:571:12:Times:12:Times:B:  However, the government not only permanently collects a 10 percent increase in social insurance 
75:2384:138219:15:15:72:517:556:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxes but also, as nominal labour cost increases, it collects substantial additional  tax revenues from 
75:2385:138323:15:15:72:370:541:12:Times:12:Times:B:personal income tax and, at some lower level, from indirect taxes. 
75:2386:138389:15:15:72:512:526:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Hence, this exercise shows that, according to the MOISEES model, it is the worker who (in the 
75:2387:138485:15:15:72:509:511:12:Times:12:Times:B:long run) suffers the full cost of the policy change. Not only because he ends up paying additional 
75:2388:138585:15:15:72:514:496:12:Times:12:Times:B:taxes but also because of the great impact that the fiscal shock has on unemployment, which lends 
75:2389:138683:15:15:72:350:481:12:Times:12:Times:B:some support to the shifting assumption used in the main text. 
75:2390:138745:15:15:72:75:466:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
75:2391:138745:15:15:72:75:451:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
75:2392:138745:15:15:72:75:436:12:Times:12:Times:B: 
75:2393:138745:15:15:72:179:421:12:Times:12:Times:B:4.D  United Kingdom 
75:2394:138764:15:15:72:501:406:12:Times:12:Times:B:Church et al. [1993] review six major macroeconometric models of the UK economy. Models 
75:2395:138852:15:15:72:517:391:12:Times:12:Times:B:discussed include both `official' models, i.e. those of Her Majesty's Treasury (HMT) and the Bank 
75:2396:138950:15:15:72:522:376:12:Times:12:Times:B:of England (BE), and models that have been developed by Oxford Economic Forecasting (OEF), a 
75:2397:139043:15:15:72:511:361:12:Times:12:Times:B:private sector organization, and by three research institutes, namely those of the London Business 
75:2398:139142:15:15:72:511:346:12:Times:12:Times:B:School (LBS), the National Institute of Economic and Social Research (NIESR) and Strathclyde 
75:2399:139235:15:15:72:521:331:12:Times:12:Times:B:University (STR). The article of Church, which has inspired this subsection, analyses the versions of 
75:2400:139337:15:15:72:518:316:12:Times:12:Times:B:all these models as of 1992/1993. The key element of such models when used to analyze effects of 
75:2401:139434:15:15:72:388:301:12:Times:12:Times:B:changes in tax rates lies in the long-run solution to the wage equation.  
75:2402:139507:15:15:72:509:286:12:Times:12:Times:B:  The role of the wedge can be assessed by writing the steady-state form of a wage equation, for 
75:2403:139604:15:19:72:219:271:12:Times:12:Times:B:example, for real wage costs as: 
75:2404:139636:19:18:72:401:252:12:Times:12:Times:B:w - p - temp = a(tind + temp + tlab) - bv(p -p* - e) + other terms 
75:2405:139694:18:15:72:526:234:12:Times:12:Times:B:where tind are indirect taxes and v(p-p*-e) is a measure of the real exchange rate scale by the import 
75:2406:139797:15:15:72:526:219:12:Times:12:Times:B:content (v) of gross output. The wedge therefore includes two components, namely a tax wedge and 
75:2407:139894:15:15:72:489:204:12:Times:12:Times:B:an import price wedge, with long-run effects α and ß. In contrast to previous versions of the 
75:2408:139988:15:15:72:527:189:12:Times:12:Times:B:models, it is now usual for the coefficients on the tax rates to be constrained to be equal. Empirically, 
75:2409:140094:15:15:72:513:174:12:Times:12:Times:B:a range of long-run wedge effects is found in the models: α = 0 in the STR and LBS models, α = 
75:2410:140189:15:15:72:518:159:12:Times:12:Times:B:0.413 in NIESR, α = 0.5 in BE and α = 0.578 in OEF. However, different from equation (3), the 
75:2411:140283:15:15:72:524:144:12:Times:12:Times:B:dependent variable in the LBS and OEF models excludes the relevant tax term, i.e. employers taxes 
75:2412:140381:15:0:72:476:129:12:Times:12:Times:B:(in the case of real wage costs) and direct taxes (in the case of real consumption wages).  
76:2413:140474:0:15:72:494:757:12:Times:12:Times:B:  It follows that different taxes have different effects. In the LBS model a lower direct tax rate 
76:2414:140573:15:15:72:507:742:12:Times:12:Times:B:produces an upward effect on wages in the long run, rather than the effects implied by the above 
76:2415:140670:15:15:72:510:727:12:Times:12:Times:B:coefficient. In the OEF model a reduction in employers taxes again upwardly effects wages in the 
76:2416:140767:15:15:72:413:712:12:Times:12:Times:B:long run, rather than to lower wages as in the case other taxes are reduced. 
76:2417:140843:15:15:72:511:697:12:Times:12:Times:B:  Table A.11 shows simulation outcomes of a cut in the standard income tax rate by 1 pence (= 1 
76:2418:140939:15:15:72:393:682:12:Times:12:Times:B:percentage point), and a 1 percentage point reduction in the VAT rate.
